<Author>kenandpaul
<Content>Enjoyable return trip but the Macao is begining to fade. We have just returned from our one week return trip to the RIU Palace Macao. After numerous visits to this resort we feel that we need to write a detailed review of our most recent experience at the Macao now in the shadows of the new RIU Palace Punta Cana.About us: We are a couple that has traveled extensively over the past 14 years in the Caribbean 2 or 3 times each year. Without a doubt we are true sun and ocean worshippers who seek out incredible beaches with powder white sand and clear Caribbean blue waters. Furthermore we enjoy personalized service, comfortable and well appointed accommodations. My partner being a private retreat chef here in Ontario, we also seek, good quality food that is presented with elegance and artful mastery. After visits to numerous islands and tropical locals we discovered Punta Cana 6 years ago and now view it as our home in paradise. In Punta Cana we have traveled numerous times to the RIU Palace Macao, once to the RIU Bambu and to the Bahia Principe Club Diamond.Planning and Booking: Our trip was planned using the very knowledgeable and professional guidance of Robyn at Itravel2000.com. Through her guidance and efforts we were able to find the best pricing and leaving at a date and time that were accommodating to our pocketbook and schedule. She answered our numerous emails promptly and with concise and accurate information. Who ever said that you did not get personalized treatment with an online travel company has never dealt with Robyn, who we will continue to book our trips with.Departure and Flight with Skyservice: We arrived at the airport within the three hour recommended timeframe and we were able to secure exit seats. I highly recommend attempting to secure these seats when you arrive at the airport (you can not pre-book these seats) as all others are completely unbearable. Our luggage was weighed and we were under weight, so no charge. Be warned baggage over is charged $10 per kilo.The flight was rather uneventful but made entertaining by the bumbling dialogue made by the head Skyservice flight attendant who stumbled through every announcement that she read. The flight was made further entertaining by the in-flight movie, not because the movie was entertaining, but rather by the further bumbling errors of the same flight attendant who first started the film then 1/5 of the way through after making an error with the sound system for one side the plane, restarted the film, then made an announcement 1/5 of the way through the movie and could not get the movie restarted so she went back to the beginning. Well if we missed anything in the beginning of the movie, we definitely caught it by the third time we saw it! The in-flight snack was a chicken quesadilla and other little packages of snacks such as cheese and crackers. All of this passes the time and tries to take your mind off the fact that you are cramped and uncomfortable and that most of the way you have someoneéˆ¥æªš elbow shoved into your side éˆ¥?and that is in an exit seat where you have the luxury of a little more room.Arrival at the Dominican Airport: As you walk off the airplane the warmth of the Caribbean night air kisses your face and you know that all of the discomfort on the airplane was definitely worth it. You exit the aircraft and walk towards the airport that is an open air thatched roof building. Get ready to smile as you enter the terminal there are two young ladies there to greet you in traditional Dominican garb who you will have your picture taken with as you pass through the entrance. These photos will be available for sale for $5 US when you leave the island a week or two later. The process to enter the island is smooth, have your passport, and blue Dominican tourist ready and wait in line to have them processed. As you wait you will be soothed by the mariachi musicians playing and the warmth of the Caribbean air. The line moves quickly. Once you have completed this process you collect your luggage and head out into the main lobby of the airport, where you will find a Sunquest rep who will point you towards the Sunquest bus which will take you to your resort. At the bus you will sign in and be given an orientation meeting invitation. At this point sit back on the air-conditioned bus and enjoy the scenery out the window and listen to the Caribbean music played. Arrival at The RIU Palace Macao: Arriving at night the week prior to Christmas we found that the palm trees that line the entranceway to the Macao a glow in hundreds of Christmas lights. The bus arrives and the luggage is taken off (make sure that your bag is taken off as the bus will likely stop at one or more other RIU properties). At reception you are given your tan wristbands, room key, safe key, towel card, and restaurant card along with luggage tags. Reception is warm, welcoming and informative and fluently delivered in English. A attentive bellhop quickly loads your luggage onto a brass luggage cart and shortly delivers your luggage to your room. The Room: We were very impressed with our third floor garden view room. We were pleasantly surprised to find we were given a corner room with three sliding balcony doors and wrap around balcony that forms into a large hexagon appointed with plantation style wooden rockers, cocktail table and drying rack. The room is appointed with two overstuffed comfortable wing chairs, small bistro table, two night stands, a large credenza that houses the mini bar, large closet that comes with approximately 10 hangers, iron and ironing board. The bathroom comes with tub/shower combination, bidet, well lit mirror, single sink and shaving mirror. The room and bathroom are outfitted with some limited toiletries (bottle of RIU shampoo/body wash, bar of RIU soap and shower cap.) You will also find a bar wall unit that houses several bottles of liquors including gin, rum gin and tequila I believe. The bar fridge has pop (Pepsi, diet Pepsi, 7Up orange soda, tonic and a large jug of water. You will also find two bottles of Bohemian Beer. Room Service: There is also a room service option for breakfast to 11:00 am and then a snack service including such items as a vegetarian sandwich, a BLT sandwich, Caesar with chicken, nachos and cheese to highlight a few.Orientation: Depending on whether you arrive in the morning or evening the orientation meeting will be held either on the day of arrival or the next morning. We always attend, but this time we wish we had not, the meeting started 20 minutes late and then all that we were told is where to find the Sunquest book that would list our departure time. Other than that the presenter struggled to explain the tours available. That was it! There was no information about the resort or the services provided.Late Night Snacks As we arrived at the resort at 11:00pm the late night snack bar was the only food option. It is located beside the pool. Here you will find a small salad bar and a small buffet serving fried chicken, fries, pizza, hamburgers, hot dogs and beans with rice. Once you are seated a waiter will come along taking drink orders. After two glasses of red wine were informed that they hand run out. Strange, we thought but decided it was because it was late at night and the waiter was on by himself he was unable to go to the main bar to get more. More on this lateréˆ¥? Piano Bar: Located next to the lobby across from the main buffet restaurant is the 24hour bar. This room definitely has a plantation feel to it, with dark, wide seated wicker chairs arranged in groupings of four around low cocktail tables. Here you can have drinks into the wee hours of the morning along with wonderful cappuccinos. Each evening you will find a variety of wonderful singers and piano players to entertain you. The last session ends around the time that the Pacha Disco opens (I believe that is 11:30). This is usually a wonderful room to sit back in and relax after spending many hours lounging in the sun.The Showroom: You enter the show room via the piano bar through huge heavy velvet drapes. The art deco dèŒ…cor continues and gives the illusion of entering the showroom of a vintage cruise ship. During the evening you will find waiters and waitresses dressed in tuxedo shirts, vests, bowties and pants. At lunch the waiters are now dressed in colorful Caribbean flowered shirts and dark pants. Kabuki: The Japanese Restaurant is one of four a la carte restaurants for Macao guest to use. You are presented with a lovely plate of sushi and a menu. Next you are given a choice of several starters, entrees and dessert. <Author>tennisguy22
<Content>Wonderful and Decadent My wife and I just returned from a five-night stay at the Riu Palace Macao. We had a wonderful visit, enjoying all aspects of the resort. It is about a one-hour nonscenic trip (32 bumpy miles) from the airport in a rather cramped small bus. The resort is truly beautiful and perfectly-maintained. It upgraded us to a very nice room facing the pool and the ocean. (It is difficult to see the ocean from almost all rooms because of all the trees.) The resort is truly all-inclusive -- with all food and drink free. One need not provide gratuities. The room is constantly supplied all types of beverages, including plenty of distilled water. (The tap water is not potable.) There is a good size private balcony with a table and chairs, that was a plus. The beds, bathroom, etc., were great. The food was fine and plentiful. The room's airconditioning was virtually silent. The staff was always friendly and well trained. The four tennis courts, which served the five-hotel Riu complex, were hard clay and just fair. A pro and his assistant were usually in attendance. One can make reservations, which are needed early in the day, for a court. There are nightly shows by different troupes, that are mostly just fair. The Folklorico Show was excellent. There are many athletic and other activities during the day. The one problem with the resort is at the pool area. People rush there early in the morning to stake out chaises with their towels, holding the chaises for the entire day, even when they are away doing other things. The resort should somehow prohibit this. The beach is great, and one can walk endlessly on it, passing other hotels. The island is sad and scrubby, and probably not very safe. We took a day-long tour to Oana Island, which cost $90 (USA) per person. It was not worth the money. It was difficult to understand the guide, and one was beseiged by vendors on the island. Its beach is not better than that of the resort. The boat rides to and from the beach were fun, with dancing and drinking on the cat return trip.

What they did was take us of the bus , sit us in the lobby bar , order us a drink (i had a Barcelo Imperial on the rocks my wife had a mojito) nice touch ,we signed our guest cards ,they gave us a quick rundown on the resort,. <Author>lewismaudlin
<Content>Hold'Em Poker with Carlos OK, I actually stayed at the RIU Palace Punta Cana next door. However, the real story was at the Macao. They have a Casino that is pretty typical for DR. The slot machines do not pay well. The blackjack is suspect. An old trick for unregulated casinos is to remove face cards from the deck and replace them with 4's and 5's. This does not mean the house will win, but it increases the houses edge significantly. Instead of a 1% advantage, the house may have a 10% advantage, thereby increasing their edge tenfold.The real story though was their TEXAS HOLD'EM game. It was a $5 sb, $5 bb, $100 buy-in no limit hold'em game. It was extremely easy. Even the regulars played very poorly. I could not believe how easy the game was. The house cut is 5% but that is easily overcome since it is a no limit game with very inexperienced players. Try the game. A nice guy at the table is Carlos who is a regular and a local. Tell him Luis sent you.

<Content>Wonderful Resort! My boyfriend and I stayed at this resort from June 28-July 5 and had a wonderful time. We booked through Apple Vacations and had a worry free trip. I read a few reviews saying the pool was small, but it seemed fine to me, even if it's not as big as other resorts. We were at the beach the entire time because the ocean breeze kept it much cooler there than at the pool. There were also plenty of activities during the day and night. We went on two excursions, one to the Marinarium and the other to Santo Domingo. I was disappointed with the snorkeling at the Marinarium. Unfortunately the coral is mostly dead and there are very few fish. My boyfriend wanted to snorkel with the sharks and rays, but I was not happy to see that they were in an enclosed cage in the middle of the ocean. We swam into the cage and were able to swim with them, but there were so many other snorkelers around and it was too crowded.The Santo Domingo trip was definitely worth the 3 hour bus trip each way. Along the way we were able to see a lot of the countryside and many small villages. The Colonial City of Santo Domingo is very pretty.........nice architecture and interesting history.A few recommendations...........men need to bring long pants for dinner and don't drink the water out of the sink in the room. The water provided at the restaurants and the bottled water in the room are fine. We didn't have any intestinal issues............we stayed away from salads and any fruits that were not peeled. Bring US cash to purchase souveniers, etc. Shop owners give discounts if you pay in cash, but no discounts for credit cards. We had a very relaxing and enjoyable vacation!

<Author>hoosier81
<Content>Loved it all! Great anniversary getaway. My husband  I spent June 19 through June 24th at the RIU Palace Maco for our 25th wedding anniversary. It was a dream vacation in paradise! We found the room to be beautiful and VERY clean. The dark wood furniture is very elegant. The beds were comfortable and view was decent, although our room was in a corner. We did not have any problems with our room and the staff called several times to ask if there were any. Whenever we asked for things such as more towels or bottled water, it came very quickly.The beach was beautiful and the nearness of the coconut palms to the ocean adds to the wonderful tropical feel. As you walk to the beach from the pool you walk through a paradise of tropical foliage covering sandy niches where lounge chairs abound. You can choose the shady tropical paradise for lounging or bask in the sun on the sandy beach. I was afraid (from the pictures) that the walk to the beach was long, but it is not and it is beautiful. We walked to each of the other RIU resorts and found that we loved the beach area of the Macao the best. The new Palace Punta Cana was pretty, but did not have the lush established palms and foliage since it is to new. The pool and swimup pool bar at the Bambu was a fun place to visit. There were more children at the other resorts. We did not do any tours but talked to people who were happy with the Samoa island trip which stops at a natural swimming pool in the middle of the ocean. We loved the variety of people from so many nationalities-lot of German, French and Spanish heard all around. We couldn't usually understand them, but love this meshing of cultures. We found several Americans to hang out with and loved meeting new people. We had American happy hour at the beachside bar on most afternoons. (Hi Mike, Mike  Janine, Chris  Jennifer, Stefani and Yolanda!) There were often events near the pool or the beach which the wonderful staff put on--contests, dance lessons (merengue, salsa, bachata) and aerobics. At night we tried the disco (Pacha) but the strobe light made us crazy. We attended the Michael Jackson show on Wed. night and enjoyed that. Our only complaint was that we didn't get much chance to use our new dance steps. The buffet restaurant is absolutely beautiful and looks like a 5 star big city elegant restaurant. We could always find plenty we liked to eat. Breakfast was our favorite. The service was always good and some of our favorite waiters spoke limited English, but we were always able to get them to understand what we wanted in some way. We vow to learn more spanish before returning! We took a small phrase book. We found that the staff varies greatly on their English and many could not understand what we asked. But, hey, we were in their country and I think we should work harder at speaking their language. Everyone was very pleasant. Tips were not expected but were graciously accepted. We ate at the Kabuki Japanese restaurant, but found the food so-so and the time it took to get through all the courses too long. We usually lunched at the beachside Caribe grill--beautiful ocean view. We have stayed in a Sandals in Jamica (Montego Bay) and this place wins, no contest. We would definitely return and stay at the Macao.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Vacation - Great Stay! Our family stayed at the Riu Palace Macao the week of June 12th. We brought 2 of our 5 kids, they are ages 12  16. They had a great time, except my daughter ended up catching a stomach virus that her aunt had at the time of our departure and ended up staying in the room for part of the trip, but what a great room to stay in! NOTE! - SHE WAS NOT SICK FROM THE FOOD OR WATER. *THE ROOM - We stayed in a suite with an ocean view and pool view. It was perfect. There is a huge balcony that runs along the side of the suite and there are 3 sliding glass doors. Beware that the doors have sensors to automatically cut off the A/C in the suite if you open the doors. Just be sure and shut the door back so the A/C will come on. The minibar has Pepsi, not Coke products. There is 7-up and club soda to go along with the alcohol dispensor on the wall. The maids come around about 3 times a day to make sure the room and balcony is swept and mopped, cleaned, re-filled with drinks, towels, etc.*THE BEACH - Outstanding is all I can say. We stayed on the beach - all the time. There is a shipwreck off of the coast and the water is very blue and clear. We purchased goggles and searched the shallow waters for pieces of old coral and shells. I've been to Cancun, and this place has the beaches in Cancun beat. *THE EURO'S - Topless women and speedos for the men at the beach and the pool. Trying to put it nicely...look the other way. You get used to it after a while, and sometimes quite comical. They are not very friendly, sometimes caught a stare and laugh from some of them sitting next to us at the steakhouse. We wondered if this was the meaning of euro trash. They mainly keep to themselves and do not respond if you walk by and say hi. But then again, I didn't go there to make friends with anyone. *THE FOOD - At it best, okay. However, you must remember that they do not cater to Europeans or Americans. They cook the way they want to cook it. They do have a lot to choose from in the El Patio. We do recommend the Steakhouse by the pool because they do have the best Cream of Tomato Soup I have ever tasted, and I don't like Tomato soup. But I have it a shot, and ate there the next night.*THE POOL - Great size - larger than you can imagine. The photos even make it look small. We did not go to swim in a pool, if we wanted to swim in a pool I would have stayed home. We went for the beach.If you go for rest and relaxation, you're at the right place. It was not boring as some of the reviews have said, even my teens had a great time. They have activities in the pool, games on the beach and they have excursions for purchase. We went on a $31.00 snorkeling tour that took us in a boat out to a coral reef and we jumped in, swam around and had a good time. Would have probably purchased a nicer $80 snorkeling tour, however we wanted to make sure the kids got the hang of it before we paid more $ for something that they could not grasp. The fish will swim up to you and swarm you while in the water. They said we could have brought a banana (we forgot) and that the fish will eat it. If you venture over to the Bambu you must have a Banana Mama. Those things are awesome. There is more of a younger crowd. I would guess that the average age at the Macao was maybe 30 something, not older-older as I had anticipated from the reviews.We will be going back, actually talking about coming back next year with the younger kids.

<Author>jinglay
<Content>Great Pre-Wedding Getaway, Food SoSo My fiance and I decided to take a vacation to Punta cana before our upcoming September wedding. I have probably read most of the reviews of most of the hotels in Punta Cana. We decided on Riu Palace Macao and were very happy with our decision - except for the food. My fiance and I are professionals in our late 20s and have traveled an average amount. I think we are past our partying days and wanted a quiet, relaxing vacation - which we got! We were there 6/2 Fri-6/5 Mon. AIRPORT: Organized, a little hot due to no air conditioning. Bring a pen for the customs card, $10 each for the tourist card. United left my fiance's luggage in Charlotte but the Punta cana staff was very helpful...the hotel was even more helpful.TRANSPORTATION: Took a cab for $28 one way. Countryside is very poor and the small road to the hotel is bumpy but it's an interesting 35-40 minute drive.CHECK-IN: No wait in front of us - we got there at 5pm. It helps to have your room reservation info on you. The staff is SO friendly. While checking in, we were brought two ice cold fruit punches. They even upgraded us to a nicer room without us asking or us giving them any $$. How nice!ROOM: The upgraded room was very nice, on the 2nd floor with the balcony facing the pool. Nice marble bathoom (the shower tub is a little narrow - room really for just one person). Very clean - I did not spot one bug. The maid came twice/day. The fridge was well stocked. We did brush our teeth with bottle water only. The first day the shower head was broken but they fixed it literally within 5-10 minutes of me calling.LANGUAGE: I speak Spanish but found the staff able to speak English well with my fiance. For those of you complaining about any language barriers, I think you should be reminding yourself what country you are in. It would be absurd for a non-American to expect me to speak their language in America, why would it apply otherwise? Bring a phrase book if you want but it's not needed.TIPPING: We tipped not because we felt we had to but because we wanted to. This country is so poor and many of the staff spend a long time at the resort before they go back to their homes. A $ is worth a lot more to them than to us. We also left packaged candy for the maids. They are very appreciative but again it's not demanded. Sometimes we would forget and found we were treated the same.FOOD: This was the only bad part of our trip. Unfortunately, we were very disappointed in the food. The buffet El Patio and buffet International (by the pool) offered up pretty much the same thing, with some variety each day. It seemed recycled, fried and the meats seemed dry. I was hoping to have some Dominican food but was disappointed. It also did not seem American - maybe it catered to Europeans? We were able to find some things we liked and stuck to that during our short stay. We did like the outdoor BBQ they had for Saturday lunch and the fiesta was fun! The pina coladas and cuba libres are also good. The Caribe Grille had similar food but with a beautiful view of the beach. We only made one reservation and this was for the Meditteraneo on our last night. The food was better but I think we were already turned off by the food by then. We met other American couples who had similar views. My fiance, the least pickiest eater in the world, even had a hard time enjoying the food. It wasn't the lack of variety, it was more the quality. But the desserts, french fries, drinks, soft served ice-cream by the bar and fruit were great! I did have a touch of a sour stomach the last day but not for long. They say not to drink the water or eat the ice but it was hard when we loved the pina coladas and hated warm drinks! We might go there again for a short trip but we will probably try another place to compare the food first. Will not go there for a long trip cuz we'd get sick of the food. CASINO: It's a small casino attached to the hotel with blackjack, 3 card poker, roulette and other games. Each night after 9pm they had a 10 person table for no-limit texas hold-em. When we played it was $1/$2 but we heard it went up to $5/$10 sometimes. It was very fun even if we lost! We heard not to play the casino's special roulette unless you want to lose a lot.BEACH: The best part of our vacation! THIS is why you go to Punta Cana. The beach is absolutely gorgeous. The white sand is soft and the ocean is a beautiful clear blue. I did not notice a lot of seaweed. The water is refreshing - cold when it was hot in the afternoon, milder later in the day. Sure there are topless women who maybe didn't need to be topless - but who cares? We tried to wait until after 2pm to go to the beach and found it more enjoyable because the breeze is strong enough to withstand the hot sun (bring sunscreen). We never had trouble with chairs - in fact, there were too many to choose from. There is plenty of chairs shaded by trees. The bar is right on the beach too. They keep the beach very clean. Make sure you find a chair that has the plastic backing to sit up with. I wish I could truly describe to you how beautiful the beach is there!POOL: Beautiful pool but why go to the pool when you have a beach? It was fun to watch some aerobics  other activities at the pool and beach.SHOPPING: Walk about 10-15 minutes to the right on the beach and you'll hit some outdoor vendors. It's a nice walk but we did not buy anything because it was mostly little handmade souvenirs, some clothes and lots of pretty paintings. Sure they try to harass you to buy their stuff, but it's their job and they need the $$. If you want to stay closer, the caribbean street on the property has some stuff but not too much. At night in the hotel lobby they have some stands for jewelry, cigars, souvenirs. Don't pay more than 1/2 of what they offer you or you will get ripped off. It did get a bit annoying having to say no or not being able to browse quietly but oh well.STAFF: WONDERFUL! Of course you will always encounter some not so nice (are all Americans nice?) but overall the staff is pleasant, very helpful and courteous. The concierge even helped to call the airport to locate our luggage (which came the next day), they called to check on the shower head and to make sure everything was ok.BUGS: I brought the Off Spray but didn't use it. Got bit a few times but my fiance did not.CLEANLINESS: Very clean! Maids are always cleaning something. The hotel is beautiful and well maintained. OTHER VISITORS: Lots of Europeans and Americans. Nobody came off as rude...there is plenty of room in the hotel areas to be by yourself. Not too many kids (we don't have any) and not sure if they have any kid-friendly activities.OTHER ACTIVITIES: Bingo in the evening, shows in the evening...we missed out on this. Some performances in the hotel lobby some evenings. We did not do any excursions.OVERALL: Courteous people, clean  pretty hotel, very nice room, quiet yet lively when you wanted, disappointing food, BEAUTIFUL beach. For a short vacation, might go back to the Riu again - will definitely go back to Punta Cana beach for a long vacation!

<Author>rugbygrrl03
<Content>First Holiday - Perfect Holiday My husband and I are a young, professional couple who finally got around to going on our honeymoon. We chose the Riu Palace Macao based on the reviews on this website, but had some reservations given the poor reviews that we noted. However, the positive reviews definitely won out. We were extremely pleased with our trip. I will try to make this review comprehensive for those who are somewhat apprehensive and are first-time travellers.1) Arrival: We booked through Apple Tours. Upon arrival to the non-air conditioned but fairly organized Punta Cana airport, we filled out our visitor cards, paid $10 each and were ushered into an air conditioned van. A pen and ready cash were helpful to speed things along. We were at the resort 45 minutes later. The countryside was incredibly poor, but still beautiful. Palm trees and blue skies abound.2) Appon arrival, our room was immediately ready. It faced the Carribean Street and was quiet. No loud neighbors. The room was large, with two double beds making a king. The maid service was twice daily. The only complaint would be that the towels seemed very harsh and worn (especially painful for sun-burnt skin). The mini-bar was kept full. We did not drink anything, but there is a daily restocking cart that makes its rounds. The mini-fridge has several bottles of beer, a gallon jug of water for drinking and brushing teeth, as well as some orange soda, lemon soda and pepsi. The TV was anti-dilluvian, but received enough English channels for an hour of Law and Order per day. The A/C in the room was intense and arctic. It was very pleasant. The safe is in the closet and you MUST have your key with you at all times. They will charge $50 if you lose it, so you best not. Put _all_ your valuables in the safe. 3) The Beach/Pool: The weather was lovely. There were a couple days of rain, but this was short-lived. It's mostly in the high 80s and humid. The beach has a nice wind. The pool deck is HOT. The pool chairs are taken up quite early, but the beach is a better option and there are plenty of recliners. The sands are lovely and there are palms for those who get burned and need some shade. There are some boats riding in the vicinity, so the waves can get pretty high. There is not much shallow water, but it seems more natural to swim in the pool, anyway. The downsides: you have to have towel cards that you hand in for two towels and get back at the end of the day. Just one more thing you can't forget in your room. The towels are clean but don't always look it. They are quite worn as well and could really stand to be updated. Some have prehistoric stains. Some are damp from being bundled together. Bring your own beach towel ifyou are particular.4) Other people: Very few children and nothing for them to do if they _did_ come. Many europeans/canadians. Topless bathing and Speedos abound, but one gets used to it.5) Staff: some English, but gestures and a dictionary help. Very friendly, try hard to please, but do work a little slower than the American pace of life. Things will get done, but it will take time.6) Food: There are several speciality restaurants available. They are reservation - only. We ate exclusively at the buffet. I found it EXCELLENT, with good variety, freshness and delicious food. We did not get sick at all, and avoided things like sea-food. The main buffett is really sufficient. Otherwise, there is a Japanese place, a Steak house and a mediterranean restaurant. I didn't see the appeal. The buffett is great. There is a poolside bar, a bar inside the hotel itself and a snack bar near the pool. All are very nice and make a wide variety of non-alcoholic and alcoholic drinks, as well as good strong iced coffee.7) Entertainment: seemed cheesy and lacking. We avoided it and made our own fun.8) Excursions: We did not take advantage. THey are about $80 per person and can vary from a trip to a private island to a inland safari to learn about Dominican life.9) Things to bring: LOTS of sunscreen, your own private pharmacy (loperamide, bismuth salicylate, tylenol, ibuprofen). Post-sunburn lotion is a must as you WILL get burned. Aloe Vera works. Bring your own toiletries if you are remotely particular. There is minimal stuff available in the rooms. Cards are also a good way to pass the time. Bring nuts or something to snack on. All that good stuff is very expensive in the shops. Bring some dollar bills for tips. It's not expected, but certainly nice and generous. People work so hard. Most of all, enjoy your trip!

<Content>Home Away From Home! My husband and I have recently spent another wonderful two weeks at the Riu Palace Macao during the first two weeks of May, 2006. This was our fifth consecutive trip to the Macao and it just gets better and better each year. There are wonderful themed lunches a few times a week, entertainment by the pool with lovely tasty, colourful and delectable dishes, along with the occasional coconut party on the beach with lively bands and musicians. There is always something to do and it's impossible to get bored.The various a-la-carte restaurants are most enjoyable, as are the regular buffet meals in the main elegant diningroom and the other restaurants. The food is incredible in variety, taste and presentation. There is never enough time or room to try everything. Ingredients are incredibly fresh and delicious and there is something wonderful to suit everyone's taste. With so many incredible restaurants to choose from, it's really a delight to stay at this resort and sample as many culinary delights as possible.The rooms are lovely and large and are kept pefectly clean by the professional staff. It's also nice to be able to relax on the comfortable rocking chairs on the balconies and enjoy the view.The Punta Cana beach is truly amazing and it's lovely to be able to walk for miles and miles on soft, white, powdery sand and take in the fragrant tropical air and gorgeous scenery; blue sky, palm trees dancing in the breeze and beautiful warm ocean.So, all in all, another perfect holiday and we can't wait until next year to be back in paradise and our home away from home!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A perfect vacation Unlike many of the reviews I read on this page, I have absolutely nothing to complain about regarding my stay at Riu Palace Macao. The hotel is beautiful with wonderfully maintained grounds that include plenty of tropical foliage. Interestingly, the grounds provide many of the niceties you'll exeperience during your stay. The flowers in your room and the coconuts they serve by the pool are all harvested right from the property. The rooms are very nice and offers small balconies (we got lucky with a corner room that afforded a large balcony). The mini-bar and perpetually re-stocked fridge are a definite plus.The beach is gorgeous. There was a constant breeze that was just enough to keep you cool. For those that want to avoid the sun, there is a large palm grove that has plenty of loungers. Both the beach and the grove are very close to the beach bar which is a great place to meet people from all over the world. There are plenty of activities (volleyball, aerobics, dance lessons) right on the beach and you can also use the hotel's kayaks, snorkeling equipment, and paddle boats for free. The excursions (many of them) are exceptionally reasonable and range from quick parasailing rides to all-day boat trips. The food was also very good. We often opted for the buffets over scheduled dinners mainly because we wanted the flexibility instead of having a reservation. The Riu's best asset, however, is the staff. They are a wonderful lot of extremely friendly and helpful people. They were very engaging and always offered an easy smile and a warm Hola. Speaking just a bit of Spanish is a help but we encountered no one that had trouble getting by even if they spoke no Spanish at all. If we had any requests at all they were attended to quickly and with great customer service. Overall, a great time. Nothing but great memories. Planning a return trip in October...can't wait!

I donéˆ¥æª› think this was status quo because the hotel staff indicated that the Palace was running at full occupancy during our stay largely due to families taking spring break.Of all the hotels on the Riu property, I would definitely say that the older crowd frequents the Riu Palace but I donéˆ¥æª› view that as a negative. I donéˆ¥æª› think tipping is necessaryéˆ¥îš¯ just like to be taken care of and I definitely came away with that feeling.Every bar that I visited on the premises sported the same level of service. So, before you go, have your expectations set at the right level and you wonéˆ¥æª› be disappointed. Whatever was lacking in foodéˆ¥î›šhe service more than made up for it. These people always greeted our party with a smile, which made the vacation very enjoyable.The ala carte restaurants were very good, although the Mediterranean establishment left a little to be desired.ACTIVITIESWe didnéˆ¥æª› partake in any of the activities although there is constantly something going on during all hours of the day. <Author>OhioBeachbaby
<Content>Our Paradise On Earth My husband and I returned from the Palace a couple weeks ago and I just found time to sit down and write this review. We were welcomed at the airport by very friendly Dominican girls, had our picture taken, and quickly got through customs, got our luggage without any problems, found our Apple Rep. (or he found us) and they escorted us directly to our comfortable air-conditioned mini-van to travel the 45 min. to the resort. I had read many reviews prior to going about the frightening ride from the airport to the resort so I expected something horrible. Actually, we have had way scarier cab rides in America! Granted, our worse roads are their best roads, but our driver was safe, although drove very fast! When we arrived at the resort, I swear we thought we were in Paradise! Beautiful grounds, very friendly and helpful staff (who knew and could speak excellent English) at the front desk. However, it does help to know enough Spanish to ask directions and be polite, which I did. Immediately, we noticed an older clientele (we are in our 40's) so we thought we would explore the nearby resorts eventually. When we arrived in the lobby, we immediately looked to the back of the resort, past the pool, and down the walkway to the beautiful Carribean. THAT was exciting to see. Although the room they gave us was on the ground floor (and I was worried about the smell of must like these reviews said), we were told to come back the following day and they would give us our requested 3rd or 4th floor room, which they did and the room was lovely. Actually, when entering our ground-level room, there was absolutely no odor or unpleasantness. It was very clean and very cool. Nothing like we thought, as we had read complaints of the air conditioning not working on this site.While there, be sure and take advantage of all the non-motorized sports you can, as it is completely free. We paddle boated in the ocean which was great! There are other things to do, but we were only there Monday through Friday. If we go again, we will definitely go for at least a week! I wish I would have taken advantage of the water aerobics in the morning and step aerobics in the evening. The instructors actually go out and recruit people to join the classes. Get ready for the most gorgeous white sandy beach ever!!! Talcum powder sand, very clean beach, with topless women and fat men in speedos everywhere!!! We love to dance, but the disco was lame. Didn't even have anyone there at 11:00 p.m. one night! Dark and smelly, I'm sorry to say. For fun, we went next door to the Bambu resort which has a pool bar and younger clientele, lots of kids though jumping off the large rocks that surround the pool. A must-do is the Maranarium snorkeling trip! SO FUN!!! We loved Jean Claude the skipper of the boat. It was like a booze cruize/snorkeling trip in one. We swam with nurse sharks and mantarays! It was so exciting. Although our bus to go there was 1 hr. late (which we sat in the rain under a little shelter at the meeting point, it was well worth it!One thing to remember...the staff is SUPER friendly, always with smiles on their faces, greeting you and constantly wanting to bring you drinks. Bring extra dollar bills to tip them; they really appreciate it and will treat you very, very well. When you see their living conditions riding to and from the airport, it so incredible that they can be so friendly, work at a lovely resort, and then have to go back home to those deplorable conditions. It just made me so sad. It is a very poor country.If you're not a drinker, you will be by the time you leave here! The tropical drinks are delicious! The buffet is interesting...lots of non-American type foods, although they have some chicken, fish, and beef that is recognizable. The salad bar had weird European-type foods on it, but the fruit is fresh and wonderful! Be careful of the hamburgers at the International place that is open late at night as they are not cooked all the way through. There is french fries there and steak sometimes, which was pretty good. We actually only ate dinner at the buffet, as there was quite a variety to choose from. Mexican night was very good...everything imaginable.Some of the reviews on here mentioned rude tourists. All the non-Americans we talked to were very friendly...even the Germans!! It was so funny at night walking through the resort at 11:00 p.m. and no one in site...older people go to bed early I guess, even on vacation! It was like we were the only ones up. The casino is open til 3 a.m., so many people were over there. It is very small and the air conditioning wasn't working. They don't have craps, just slot machines (that don't work half the time), Blackjack, Roulette, and video poker. You should barter down the price on Carribean Street. The bands were fun to listen to. The weather was great, although it rains a little each day. There is really no excuse not to have a good time there....a vacation is definitely what YOU make of it! We will return to Punta Cana, but probably to a different resort next time.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Second class resort If you're use to Sandals or cruiselines then this may not be for you. The buffet food was usually either cold or under cooked. We found the Kabuki and Steak house to be the best choices for evening meals with the food above average although you had to make a reservation each morning. English is a new language and communications was sometimes a challenge but the staff were receptive and normally helpful. The beaches are nice but high winds kept us on shore most of the time. The rooms are large but the beds are quite firm. Pool service for drinks is somewhat slow and the pool seemed to be the smallest of the RIU resorts in the area. The palace caters to the more laidback crowd which is primarily european, for the party crowd go to the RIU Bamboo. We didn't take any tours but received poor feedback from another couple regarding the half day snorkling excursion with the nurse sharks. Their most popular tour takes you to a grade school and into an average families home, not your usual tour fair to say the least. The casino is quite small and open only in the evenings. I came back $75 ahead on the 25 cent slots so it was okay by me. All-in-all, it was okay with nothing really standing out or any excursion a must do. Most things seeming to be just short of our expectations which may be due to our Sandals and cruiseline experiences. IF you want a first class experience then pay up and goes elsewhere. This would be a good first time trip for the budget minded travelers.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very decent holiday My wife and I spent a seven day holiday at Riu Palace Macao, Punta Cana week of January 14th, 2006 with my parents and infant daughter. To put in context, we tend to vacation once per year in south (e.g Cuba, DR, or Mexico). Was very satisfied with this hotel. Yes, when the brochures state 5 stars, we are not talking London, Paris, NYC or Toronto equivalents so let's rein in expectations which seem to skew other reviews I have read on this hotel.1) Very good food. We enjoyed the variety of the buffet for breakfast and dinner. Snack bar for lunch was ok. Good theme nights which added to variety - handing out cigars to all guests, special cocktails, etc. Yes, you had to indicate whether you wanted to eat at 630pm or 830pm however there seemed to be flex within this. We thoroughly enjoyed the Caribe Grill (one of the non-buffet restaurants) for dinner one evening for more traditional sit-down dinner. 2) A/C...as other reviews note this is a slightly older, classical design hotel so the A/C does not cool your hotel room down in 5 minutes. However, we left our system on virtually all the time and found the interior room temp cool and pleasant. Actually, was nice to have a system which was totally silent. (Frankly, if it is that bad, there are ceiling fans which you can activate which we found made it too cool). 3) Our room was well maintained and clean; no problems with the bathroom other than the odd temporary shortage of decent hot water. Well stocked mini-bar which was at our disposal as part of package. Me thinks you will be hard pressed to find that kind of amenity free of charge in any locale in N America; was nice to indulge without having to complete a mini-bar inventory sheet!4) Staff were really very friendly and helpful yet not over-bearing. We found the folks at reception accommodating particularly when we had requests relating to our infant. 5) As other reviews note, this is not party central. Seemed to be slightly more mature guests primarily from US, Germany and Canada. Actually, this worked out well for us as we have never had more folks fawning over our 10 month old infant!...surrogate uncles, aunts, grandparents, etc. If you are looking for a very lively environment, you may prefer to opt for an alternate as this may not fit the bill.All in all, we found this to be very solid value for money and would quite happily return if we were venturing back to Punta Cana.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Punta Cana is Beautiful! My boyfriend and I just returned from our 1st trip to Punta Cana (Jan 14th - Jan 22nd). I must admit that I was skeptical going to a 3rd world country - I was not sure what to expect. Our trip was through Apple Vacations. When we arrived in Punta Cana we were greeted by our Apple representative. We were taken to the hotel via a bus - the hotel is approx. 40 minutes from the airport. When we pulled up in front of the hotel - it is breathtaking - the lobby is completely open - Palm trees everywhere. We were taken into the bar area where we were provided with a fresh glass of fruit juice, our room keys, towel cards, and a brief review of the hotel's accomodations. They must stress 10x's - DO NOT DRINK THE TAP WATER. The rooms are nice - plenty of closet and drawer space. A nice size balcony with two rocking chairs, a table and a bathing suit dry-rack. It is not the most modern room, however we looked at as we are only using it to bathe and sleep so it worked for us. It was clean - the maid came in and provided us with fresh towels every day and refilled the fridge, which has Pepsi, Diet Pepsi, Beer, Shasta Orange soda, bottled water, Tonic Water.The room also has bottles of liquor on the wall - we didn't use it - I think that it had rum, scotch, whiskey and something else - it's included so use it if you want. They will refill it if you empty the bottles.The pool is nice - the water was a bit chilly, but once you got in - you were used to it. You will have towel cards that you will use to get beach towels and when you return the towels at the end of the day you get the card back for the following day. The lounge chairs fill up quickly in the morning - people tend to get their spots early and although they may not be using the chairs - they will leave shoes, etc. on them to save them. Waiter's walk atound all day and will take drink orders and bring them to you. We brought $100.00 in one dollar bills - hand them a $1 or $2 and you get special treatment. The staff is always looking to get people involved in activities - water aerobics, regular aerobics, dancing, darts, BINGO, etc. They play Volleyball on the beach. I personally found the beach better - the ocean water was like bath water - very warm. There is plenty of lounge chairs. The water was a little rough. Lot's of topless women - in fact, the women that could have went topless or wore thong bathing suits didn't and the ones that should have kept their suits on where the ones that were showing the goods! After a day or two - it's no big deal - seen one - seen them all.We had excellent weather - warm and sunny everyday. When it did rain it was for a short period of time and then the sun came out. The food at the main buffet inside the hotel was the best. Breakfast was typical breakfast food - pancakes, french toast, bacon, eggs, vegetables, 10 kinds of fruit juices, fruit bar, omelette station, bread bar, cereal, yougart. Lunch and Dinner at the buffet were just as good - if you can't find something that you like - then there is a problem. So much to choose from and it's actually decent food. The only thing that I stayed away from was the milk (too thick), the salad dressings, and the yougarts. They have theme nights in the main buffet as well - Mexican night was great (Tacos, Nachos, etc). We ate at the Steakhouse one night during our stay for dinner - you have to make your reservations early in the morning when you head to the main buffet for breakfast. There is either a 6:30 or 8:30 seating. We chose the 8:30 seating for all of our meals - it worked out best for us - we didn't have to rush off the beach. The Steakhouse was good - steak and baked potato, salad, appetizer and dessert. The wine is not the best quality, but it is okay. The beer (Presidente) is always nice and cold - very refreshing!We also ate at Caribe - the dinner was very good, however they rush you - one plate right after another - as soon as you are done one course, they are placing the 2nd one down in front of you - I think we ate our meal in less than a 1/2 hour and we had an appetizer, soup, salad, meal and a dessert. We did not eat at Kubuki (Japenese)although we heard that it was very good. If we were at the pool during the day - instead of going to the main buffet inside the hotel we ate at Mediterrean (outside buffet). Typical lunch food - pizza, salad, burgers, chicken, fruit, dessert table. The nice thing about this place is that they serve food from 12-6pm. The main buffet's lunch ends at 3:00pm so they can get ready for dinner. The show's were okay - we saw their rendition of GREASE and Michael Jackson. It's no LAS VEGAS, but it's Entertainment!The Casino is a joke - I like to gamble and I spent $60.00 my first night in their casino and got it out of my system - I had no interest in going back. The slot machines are outdated and don't pay out - not sure what the deal is with the tables, although we were told to stay far,far away from the Progressives -it can get you in a lot of trouble!The shopping is okay - you definitely need to haggle and get the cost down. I wouldn't spend 1/2 of what they were asking for on certain items. $40.00 for a beaded necklace that you can get back in the States for $15-$20. I did breakdown and buy a magazine for the beach and spent $9.00 for it. It's normally a $3.00 magazine. I can't stress enough - bring plenty of sunscreen - we ran out mid-trip and had to buy more on Carribean Street - we took three regularly sized bottles to the register and was told that it was $64.00. We could have gottem the same three bottles at Walmart for $15.00. You can get a couple of American TV stations, which is nice if you are in your room early and just want to wind down and watch television. I was able to watch Judge Judy, Law and Order, there was a movie channel as well ESPN sports for the sports fanatics.If you want to blow-dry (there is a blow-dryer in the bathroom, however it is not the most powerful)or curl your hair, bring an adaptor or the hotel will give you one ($5.00 deposit that you will get back at the end of your stay). My cell phone worked the 1st day and then I was not able to get a connection - we purchased 16 minute phone cards for $10.00 USD from our APPLE agent that sits in the lobby and used them to check in with family. The staff is wonderful - everyone is very, very friendly and accomodating. We left tips every night for our waiter at dinner and tipped periodically during the day. Again, it's all inclusive so you don't need to tip, however we wanted to give a little something. You will see just how hard these people work. We learned that they work 11 days on and then they get to go home for three days and visit with their families. We met one waiter who travels seven hours one way on his three days off to see his family before having to return to the hotel again. My only complaint is that we had a late flight out (9:30pm). You will need to be ready to leave for the airport three and 1/2 hours prior to your flight. We needed to check out of our room at 12:00 noon - I did not feel comfortable leaving my luggage in the lobby of the hotel for six-seven hours, but we didn't have a choice. I had to walk around with my purse, and carry on bag that had my jewelry, i-pod, DVD player, etc. that I was not leaving in the lobby. When we asked the night before for a late check-out we were told that it would not be a problem and to check back with them the following day - when we checked back we were told that all the rooms were taken and we would not be able to have a room. We then asked about a courtesy room to shower before our flight as we wanted to spend time at the pool/beach. Again, we were told that they would accommodate us and to come back at 4:00pm - when we asked about the room at 4pm -we found out that there was only one room and that there was 8 people ahead of us waiting to clean-up as well. We finally were able to get a room at 5:15.Otherwise, vacation was great - would definitely go back. Would probably try a different hotel just to see what else is out there. The age group in this resort was older - mostly couples and families with children. We are in our late 30's and we were fine with it. If anyone wants to contact me, please feel free.

<Content>Very Satisfied We had a great stay at the Riu Palace.Rooms, facilities, food and service provided exactly as we expected for this type of resort. <Content>Typical higher-level all-inclusive Christmas week at the Riu Palace Macao made for a very relaxing holiday. We went with a large, multi-generational family group, and everyone was satisfied. Compared with other all-inclusive resorts in this price range, the resort would be rated average or better in most areas, other than the food in the specialty restaurants, which was awful. However, if you have older people with you, who are easily overwhelmed or perhaps a little confused, this resort is very easy to navigate, as there are ramps and elevators and it is not very big and complicated as there is only one building with guest rooms in it.

<Author>TorontoLove2Travel
<Content>Older Property But Very Well Kept and Great Service My husband, teenage son and I stayed at the Riu Palace from December 9 - 16th. If you are going to travel outside the resort, don't rent a car ... hire a taxi and hang on for dear life! Francisco from the front desk at the Bambu is very helpful about where to go outside the resort.. one afternoon after his shift he took us into Higuey for the afternoon and showed us around.. a definite eye opener. Some of the living conditions (ok most) for the Dominicans are poor if not sad, but they are the nicest, friendliest most laid back people and you are definitely welcome off the resort. If you're going on vacation and looking for perfection then you might as well stay home. We've stayed in many Punta Cana resorts as well as the Mayan etc ... you're in a third world country and their 5 star is not the Toronto Hilton by any means, but if you want a nice place with good food, fun entertainment, friendly staff, relaxing beaches (you can always find a chair) .. then you'll enjoy it here ...

My suggestion - ask to speak to the General Mgr of the Rui chain who is onsite to get results. Also, if you have kids and expecting the kids camp at the Bambu to be functional, forget it. This was the worst kids club I have encountered - open only from 10-12, 3-5pm with minimal supervised activities. Compare this to the Barcelo Maya - excellent hotel, service, mini club. Apart from the AC, Front desk waisting our time, and older hotel being old, its ok. We had other issues as well - toilet broke twice, and a water leak from the room above. Service is excellent, drinks great, food is not bad, beach nice. Email me lagunahome@hotmail.com if you want more info.

<Author>jewcpink
<Content>RIU palace is more like Children's Palance We stayed at the RIU Palace for 4 nights. Word of caution (in case you aren't told) do not just let anyone port your luggage after you get it from the claim area. We were transported to the resort via the Apple Vacations shuttle. During our ride, the travel specialist onboard explained how long it would take to get to our resort, the activities we could choose from and book through our on-site apple representative, and answered all of our questions. Although the ride to our hotel was a little frightening, it was attributed to the fact that they do not have paved roads or stop lights/signs in the rural town areas which you travel through to get to the resorts. When we arrived at our hotel, we were told not to let our luggage out of site until it was in the hands of the porter who immediately greeted us when we stepped foot on the sidewalk. I must say that when I saw the hotel, I was impressed. There was a HUGE floral and tropical plant arrangement on a glass table in the lobby and everyone at the desk greeted us with a smile. The lobby was furnished with beautiful bamboo and rattan furniture. The clothing store, jewelry store and convenience store onsite was suprisingly reasonably priced. We were given our room numbers, keys and a run down on the amenities offered. One complaint that I have is that the elevators are VERY small, sweltering hot and sometimes get stuck. Upon entering our room, I was pleasantly surprised at the cherry wood and marble detail. The enormous closets were much more than I expected. There was a towel that was twisted to form a heart and sprinkled with fresh flowers on our table top. Word of caution...do not pay the extra $ for an ocean view room. There are NO ocean view rooms. I believe they call it partial ocean view, but the trees block the view of the ocean from where the hotel sits. We chose the garden view which gave us a beatiful view of the pool area...which allows you to see the all the speedos in the morning as you eat breakfast. All of the rooms have a patio/deck that includes rocking chairs and tables. It's nice to sit out there and listen to the waves crash into the shore. We dined at a few of the restaurants, but found everything to taste pretty much the same. The desserts were a little disappointing. None of the pastries were sweet and some of the fruit, suprisingly, was not sweet. I must tell you that the breakfast buffet at the palace is AMAZING. Cook to order omelettes, pancakes, different choices of meats and cheeses, cereal and fresh fruit juices were offered. They offered a wide variety of breads with fresh sweet cream butter...YUMMY!!! I am definately a shopper, so my first priority was to venture outside of the resort to see the REAL Dominican Republic. My husband told the concierge of our desires, so he set us up with a driver and we visited a place called Bavarro. I don't remember the rest of the name, but they had stores that were the equivalent of our shopping centers. Be prepared to firmly say no if you do not want to enter a store or you will be badgered by the locals to enter their store. Also, watch out for the little children that may follow you around and beg you for money. You may want to give, but please keep in mind that the people here are well aware that you are a tourist and they know how to play on that. We did find some very nice pieces for our home and the statues are amazing and cannot be found in the states. If you are a cigar aficianado, the cigar shop sells authentic cigars and will even offer you a cigar to sample. They make this drink called mamajuana...please don't confuse this with the illegal stuff nicknamed mary jane they are definately not the same and mamajuana is legal. It is a drink made from honey, red wine, rum and the bark from a special tree. Very good, but VERY STRONG- try it- you'll see (maybe even see double). We laid on the beach and tried not to stare at the many different sites, such as 90 year old men in circulating prohiting speedos and 60 year old women indulging in topless bathing. All I have to say is...you gotta see it for yourself!!! The Riu offer nice thick towels for the beach and comfy cushions for the chairs. The bars are close to the beach front so a cool tropical drink is only steps away. The nightly shows are packed full of entertainment with well trained dancers and singers and much merengue. The casino is small, but my husband really enjoyed playing poker. We couldn't understand why the dealers are not real personable like they are in Las Vegas, but found out later that they are not permitted to accept tips. That could be the reason, who knows? If you go, please ask for Reymundo at the front desk. He is the absolute best. He speaks many different languages and should be the model for a superior customer service provider. Now to my complaints: We never received our complimentary refreshment plate, which is supposed to be delivered to your room when you arrive. One of the male workers kept making passes at me and approached me with alcohol on his breath. He even tried to kiss me and followed me to the door of the elevator. If you are a woman, please be careful. I informed management who took my complaint seriously and immediately handled it. One last complaint is that the RIU is not 24 hour inclusive regarding food. Make sure you eat a full meal before the restaurants close or you will just be hungry. The only thing offered overnight is diced peanuts. There are definately TOO many kids at the RIU. I was amazed at how many children were at the show where the girls were dancing (butt cheeks hanging out) and smoke was so thick you could cut it. It's not a bad thing to have kids at the resort, but the children there during our visit were very unruly- jumping off of sculptures, running through the halls...etc. WORD of CAUTION: DO NOT TRY THE VENUS SPA!!! They try to cheat you. I paid for a particular service for my husband and they gave him something totally different and tried to say that it was just an oversight but I should still be happy because he got something. It was only after I talked to the manager of the hotel that the manager of the Venus Spa offered me $20 back. Instead of bringing it to me, she made me walk and get it. Unprofessional in my opinion. Overall, our trip to the RIU was nice and although we will be visiting the DR again in a couple months, we will probably try another resort.

This resort does not have botteled water they serve you water in an 8oz cup. many times there is no ice. towel service at the beach ends at apx 4pm so if you plan to go swimming after this get a towel early. I was in the casino and playing roulette and they make a lot of mistakes  quickly removing chips without payment and very poor math skills but they did say they were mistakes! If you are an american you will get a room on either side of the hotel. The ocean front rooms are for europeans. The rooms are very nice and also cleaned well daily. mini bar was stocked at least once a day.there is not always room service if you call to early before 7 am or after 4 pm nothing. and there is not food 24 hours a day as stated. We did not get sick but met many who were. We did get bad hart burn. so overall i would say in apple terms a 3 or 4 red apple would be just. this is not what i paid for. the build is very nice but airconditioning is very very limited. I could go on in writing this review but the more i think about this place the more i get discouraged.

<Author>garyandsue515
<Content>Wonderful Resort! This was 4th trip to Riu Palace Macao and it was better than our fist visit. We left for the D.R. on July 13th after debating whether or not to cancel due to the impending arrival of Hurricane Emily. Fortunately, Emily went south and the weather was wonderful for the entire week. Hotel rooms have been refurbished and are absolutely spotless. I like to request a room on the 2nd or 3rd floor to avoid the musty smell that has been reported, but did have a first floor and there was no problem with odors at all. One night the maid had put sheets on the beds that were nubby and kind of painful, but we pulled them off and they were replaced with fresh ones the next day. Pillows were in need of replacement, but since there were about 6 in the room we had a selection. The food was varied and very good. We traveled with our 13 year old nephew who is (at best) an extremely picky eater and he was able to survive the week with no difficulty. (plenty of pizza, pasta, bread and ice cream) Against my better judgement, we ate at the Steak House restaurant expecting steaks to be the tough, caribbean meat you usually find. WRONG!! They were very good...We ate and drank everything and no one became ill at all. They sprayed the property every am (very early) for mosquitos. Bugs were not a problem at all. There was the occasional millipede in the hall, but that was no big deal. Alcohol was premium and plentiful. THE BEACH is the best. Soft white sand, long, wide and full of palm trees for shade. Never a problem finding a beach chair. We've been to many many beaches, this is one of my favorites. The swimming pool is not huge, but very clean with continuous fountains. I personally hate swim up pool bars so it was a blessing not to have one. If someone feels that is necessary, just go to one of the nearby other Riu Hotels which do have swim up pool bars. We traveled with Apple Vacations out of Baltimore and they did a wonderful job as well. One word of caution....When departing from Punta Cana Airport make certain to check, re-check, and tripple check your departure gate as they change them without notice. It would be easy to miss your flight if you do not keep up to date.All in all, really great hotel and we will continue to return. Please feel free to email me if you have any questions or concerns.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Our new home away from home As a previous travel agent and flight attendant I have stayed in all sorts of properties from the U.S., Mexico and Europe. I must admit that not only I, but my husband and my 14 year old daughter are used to staying at the best hotels when we go someplace or we do not go at all. And we don't get into eating at Mc Donalds while we are on vacation. This was one of the first vacations that I had actually considered cancelling because I had read alot of very mixed reviews of not only the hotel but vacationing in the Dominican Republic. Thank goodness that we did not decide to cancel. The Riu Palace Macao is exactly as it is described and then once you settle in it becomes even more. If you are looking for Disney World or a 24 hour party, this is DEFINATELY not the place for you. However if you want total class and a really nice upscale family vacation where you actually get the chance to talk to eachother and truly enjoy the real Caribbean experience of relaxing while listening to the wind blowing through the coconut palms and love the sound of the waves gently breaking on the beach, with the option for all the water sports you can handle, this is it. There is shopping nearby too. The hotel is like a step back in time, almost like a Morrocan palace that might have been in some Hemmingway book. The hotel is true Caribbean with dark woods and marble. Absolutely the cleanest hotel I have ever stayed at. Not 1 bug! The staff is absolutely charming and due to the fact that it is not a monster sized hotel the staff all know you within the first couple of days you are there. Anything you could possibly need to ask for is taken care of and then followed up on by the asst. mgr. Infact, one day I had really overdone it and become dehydrated and sick to my stomach, enough for the mgr. to have to call the doctor. Larissa, the asst. mgr took my husband personally to the manager of all the restaurants, introduced them, explained that I was upstairs in bed sick and that at any time no matter what time of the day or night that they make me anything that I wanted and would'nt even let him carry it to my room!!! Who does that??? I can even say that I have experienced a Dominican doctor and have nothing but good to say about that too! Nothing some electrolites could'nt handle. For the first time at an all inclusive I had an assigned dinner time, thinking I would hate it but we loved it! I loved being able to pick what seating I wanted for dinner as I had the same table every night and the same waiter and waitress who knew exactly what we drank and who we were. We never had to jockey for a table. If we wanted to swith times we could . Even better was the no limited nights to your dinners at the specialty restaurants like at other all inclusives.Our standard dinner staff greated us every night and took care of everything we needed and never rushed us. We had the same waiter and waitress every night. They addressed us with smiles and a friendly greeting everytime they saw us. They become your friends. And even if they aren't really glad to see you, you would never know it. The staff as a whole are the hardest working and happiest staff I have ever come across. I have to attribute this to the philosophy of Riu Hotels first for having such high standards and secondly for the Dominican people and proper staffing. EVERY night the asst. mgr, Larissa was in the dining room with a pad and pen, stopping at each table taking the time to speak to every guest, meeting all of us, asking questions about their stay and then writing down anything that someone might like changed or noting something that made someone unhappy and then actually looked into whatever the problem was and fixed it by the next time she saw you! (Effortlessly) She never stopped working, even when her husband was home with her 3 year old extremely ill. In comment to the Americans who have problems with the type of food that is prepared, please keep in mind that you are not in the United States. Also remember that this is not an American Hotel. Riu Hotels is run by a company based in Spain. It's primary clientele is from Europe. Therefore if I had to describe the food I would have to say it has a strong European influence but also is mixed with some Caribbean/Dominican. For those die hard U.S. travelers there is pizza served all day long as well as roast beef and turkey in the dining room for dinner. Pancakes, ham, sausage,cereal, toast plus lots of other European type choices for breakfast. If you can't find something to make your stomach happy here, considering that you are where you are, you might as well stay home. The difference if the food is part of the total experience. This is a very upscale hotel in a very POOR country. Have we had better food in other countries? Yes. But I really have no complaints nor did my husband whose family are caterers.To wrap things up, my family and I absolutely loved our vacation form our tennis games in the morning, the smiling faces at the front desk and restaurants, the entertainment at night and during the day by the pool, the most beautiful beach I have ever seen, the landscaping, my soft sheets and most importantly, how the entire staff made you feel. You were'nt just a room number in a huge all inclusive. You were a GUEST. And they made you feel that way. Some people just get it and some people it just does'nt click with. Infact I was not surprised to learn that about 75% of the Riu guests are rreturn customers every year. As I said, you eiter get it or you don't. It is BECAUSE of the way we were treated that we will continue to return. Infact just yesterday I recieved an e-mail from the asst. mgr. just saying hi and checking on the status of my Riu Club Card. We talk about our families and our lives as if we had known eachother for awhile. We have never experienced this at any other resort before. If you are expecting an American Holiday this is not it. If you love meeting people from other countries and sharing cultures in the laps of luxury this is it with total class... just not the flashing lights and Imax theatres of Cancun and Las Vegas. Not that they are'nt great too. It's just not that kind of vacation. It's a classy non-rowdy hotel. Kindof that old money feel but not stuffy. I am 41. My husband is 43 and my daughter is 14. It's not just for a bunch of old people. The staff is there for all ages and all cultures. You just have to remember you're not in Kansas anymore and enjoy the Dominican people. We did and are so glad we went. We are already trying to figure out when we can get back.
