<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We'll DEFINITELY return again!!!!! :))) My husband and I honeymooned at the Palace from 6/27-7/1. Prior to leaving, we read dozens of reviews from other past guests...all I can say is listen to everything positive about this place!!! This place is absolutely beautiful...not perfect, but the natives try their hardest to make it perfect! If this is your first time on a resort, like us, you will fall in love with this one. If you have previously traveled to other resorts, you will fall in love with this one. I am going to break my review down in some categories:SCALE OF 1 to 10FOOD: SCORE 8 Loved the fish, grilled veggies, and abundance of fruits. There were some questionable dishes, however, what can you expect when you are in another country? I say, if you keep an open mind, and think outside of the box, you will be satisfied with the food. The best part was that we didn't have to cook for ourselves for 4 days! :)SERVICE: SCORE 10This was one of the best parts of the trip! Understanding that DR is a very poor country, you'll be amazed by the service that the natives give despite their circumstances. They gave wonderful service with a smile, and they expected nothing in return. I can say that we spent a nice portion of our money on tips (because we wanted to, not because we had to). Also, I saw security checking the bags of the cleaning ladies before they left off the resort to go home. ROOMS: SCORE 8I can say that the pictures on this website do not do justice for the rooms. The rooms are much larger in person. Ours was an ocean-view suite, but because we were on the 2 floor, we didn't have much of a view of the ocean, but we had an excellent view of the pool and garden area. We had 2 queen-size beds put together to make one huge loveboat. :) The bathroom was very nice, and the balcony was large. oh...you can easily dial home by dialing 9+1+area code and #...for a $2.00/minute charge. :(One negative that we experienced in the room was small ants and almost invisible little spiders, but we wiped the the dresser with disinfectant wipes, and had the hotel spray the room, and we didn't have a major problem with it later. Since I am a country girl, that really didn't bother me. It was kind of expected on an island with so much vegetation. Also, they kept the room stocked with sodas and liquor. One more thing, if you keep your towels and washclothes on the racks in the bathroom, they will assume you are willing to re-use the same. You have to put them on the floor if you want a new one. At the end of our trip, after we had to check out at 12:00 noon, the hotel was kind enough to give us a temporary room until we were scheduled to leave the resort at 4:00pm. I guess this was a room set aside for that purpose because it was very small. The view was non-existent, and the the furniture was not in the best condition. This let us know that our original room was excellent because it could have been worse! Guess you get what you pay for! :)POOL: SCORE 7I did not go into the pool at our hotel, which was beautiful with 3 fountains in it, however everyone else looked as though they were really enjoying it (topless and all!). I did go into the pool next door to the right of the hotel, but, honestly, I wasn't too crazy about it because there was some yellow stuff and other debris floating on the edges. At one point and time, I took in a little water...the next day my stomach was a little queazy...a little immodium AD and 7-up cured that problem! The pool at the Palace did not look dirty from where I could see.BEACH: SCORE 10Plenty of chairs, space...Again, I am not a swimmer, so I didn't get the full effect, but my husband, who is a fish, was in absolute awe. I thought the water was a little rough, but he thought it was just right! I did get use to the water after a while. I enjoyed sunbathing on the beach more than anything else. Being a beautiful, dark-skinned African-American woman (and definitely a minority at this resort), I found it wonderful to stand out from the rest of the crowd. I took advantage of the topless opportunity (that of which I would never do in the states!) Everyone was very respectful, and no one gawked, but I did notice some admirers! :) I can say that this place really did give me more appreciation and love for my own body and skin, especially seeing all the different people who were not afraid to share their bodies as well.EXCURSIONS: SCORE 10If you are fortunate enough to go on the OUTBACK SAFARI and have NACHO as your tour guide, you will have the opportunity to learn so much about DR that you probably did not know before visiting. This excursion is well worth the money (approx $79/person). We were able to travel into the country side, and see how some of the Dominicans live on a daily basis. If you go, make sure to purchase some of the fresh coffee. Also, despite how some others say to take something for the local kids, NACHO explained to us that, not only is it against the law, but also they discourage tourists from giving money, candy, toys, etc. to the kids because it promotes begging, and they want their children to understand the importance of working hard to earn their money, etc. BARGAINING:Make sure you get the price that YOU want to pay for anything that you purchase there. The hotel prices are not really negotiable, but everywhere else (including high-priced Caribbean Street) can be negotiated...start ridiculously low and then move up. Be absolutely serious about it. Remember the exchange rate right now is like 29 pesos to $1.NIGHTLIFE: SCORE 4We enjoyed Carnival on one night on Caribbean Street, but other than that, nightlife was a little non-existent at the Palace. You see people walking around, but it wasn't nothing to write home about. This place is about pure relaxation. If you're looking for a place to party...this is NOT it, but it is a place to enjoy the person you are with.DRINKS: SCORE 8I'm not much of a drinker, but I had my full of drinks! :) They didn't seem very strong; however if you asked them to add a little something extra in it, they were more than happy to oblige. My husband really loved the Presidente beer.OTHER VACATIONERS:Pretty much this place is filled with Europeans (Germans, French, English, etc...). It was great to see other Americans, but on the other hand, it was very nice to observe the ways of the other nationalities and cultures. We could learn a thing or two from each other...some of them could learn to loosen up a little, and some of us could learn to be a little more reserved when appropriate. :) However, if you make eye-contact and smile at some of the Germans, you may be able to get them to break their stoic facial expressions. SPA: SCORE 7We received a 30 minute couples massage. They mainly focused on our backs. I've had better massages, but maybe if we paid for more time, it would have been worth writing home about. AIRPORT: SCORE 9We were a little confused at first only because of the language barrier; however, we quickly figured out what we needed to do from other knowledgeable Americans. Then we were met by an Apple rep who lead us directly to our transport van (about 45 minute ride to resort).NEGATIVES:some mosquito bites (but i'm still here to write about it)heat rash (but i'm still here to write about it)spiders/ants in the room (but i'm still here to write about it)missed the lobster dinner on friday night (but...well i'm still a little upset about that one...BUT i'm still here to write about it :)ADVICE:pack lightly, it's very hot and humidif you're of a paler complexion, take a black bathing suit, and if you're of a darker complexion, take a white bathing suit...the contrast on the skin is amazing! :)take plenty of sunscreen (AAs, too)don't forget meds (tylenol, immodium, etc)don't swallow the water (not even the pool water)guys take plenty of t-shirts (it's very humid)TAKE SMALL BILLS ($1, $5, $10) - you can lock your cash in your room safe...we never used our VISA, and our large bills were used for the excusion onlystay for atleast 7 days, 4 was too short for usOPEN YOUR MIND, AND ENJOY YOUR STAYTREAT THE STAFF WITH ALL DUE RESPECT...THEY DESERVE IT!!! :)peace!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Rollercoaster at the Palace I just returned from a 7 day vacation/honeymoon at the Riu Palace (June 8-15). My fiance and I took 24 of our closest friends and family down there for our wedding, which was absolutely beautiful. We got married on the beach, and with the help of the wedding coordinator at the Palace, Magnolia, everything turned out just as I had imagined. We were upgraded to a suite upon our arrival, and things were looking pretty good. However, from then it was like a roller coaster. We didn't arrive at the Palace until 5:30, and we were starving. But because all of the restaurants were getting ready for the 6:30 dinner, we weren't able to eat anything. Every night all of the restaurants have two dinner seatings, at 6:30 and 8:30, ONLY! We had three kids traveling with us, an 11 year old, a 6 year old, and a 21 month old. At 6:30, it is just way too early to eat, and at 8:30 it is too late. The same night of our arrival, we were ALLOWED to eat in the main buffet restaurant at 8:30, however once we got down there, we were refused to be let in, because all the men had on shorts, and men have to wear pants to eat in this restaurant, where there is little to no air conditioning. We were at the beach where it was 90+ degrees, why would we bring pants? The people there weren't even nice about it, they were very rude and said that the guys could possibly BORROW some from the front desk! If not, then you just don't get to eat, because they don't allow you to take food out of the restaurants and there is no room service available (only in the mornings from 7 am to 10 am). Luckily the front desk had some horrible navy blue polyester pants in various sizes that the guys were able to put on for the duration of dinner! To close on the restaurants, the food is horrible, so make sure you take plenty of snacks, and make sure that you make reservations EVERYDAY to eat, or else you won't get to! One night we went to one of the restaurants without reservations, and were turned away, with only 7 people in the restaurant, because they didn't have enough food!! I have never been to an All Inclusive that didn't have enough food! Also, my new husband got so sick after eating some strange looking beef (Dominican mystery meat). He threw up for two days and then ended up eating Pringles, Doritos, and Snickers that he bought from the store for the rest of our trip! The wait staff is pretty good, as long as you're tipping, they will come around regularly to check on you and bring you more drinks. The beach bar is definitely the best; besides its location, they are the only bar with frozen drinks and the atmosphere just can't be beat!The beaches there are so beautiful, white sand and turquoise water. They are a lot of activities that can be booked down at the beach, and those are pretty much the only ones available. The Palace crowd tends to be European and senior citizens. It is not much of a party place and they don't offer very many activities in itself. The pool there is very nice, as is all of the scenery; great views everywhere that you look!The days before our wedding, we were able to get pretty much anything that we wanted from the front desk; however afterwards, it was a different story. Some of the people who worked there would pretend that they couldn't speak English, even though we had talked to them before, like when there was a problem. On the day that my family left, some of them left their carry-on bags behind the front desk, and then when they went back to get them, stuff was missing out of them: CD players, makeup, etc., and when they were confronted about the missing items, the staff got very ugly and used very foul language to express themselves! The cleaning staff at the Palace is the best that I have ever seen. They are the friendliest ones there, they do an awesome job, and are VERY trustworthy!Most of our group is pretty young, 20's-30's, and we were hoping that this resort would be a little more happening. It is very much a place to go and relax. If you go with a group, you can liven it up, or if you're lucky, you'll meet some other people there your age to hang out with. The Palace is definitely nicer than the other Riu hotels in Punta Cana, but it is definitely not a 5-star resort. I have been to many other resorts in Cancun, Cozumel, Puerta Plata, Cabo San Lucas, Puerta Vallarta, etc., which were nicer and they may or may not have been 5-star. The Palace is very proud of their 5-star status, as they bring it up anytime they can, but I'm not quite sure that their stars are the same as in the US!If you have any questions or would like to see pictures, please email me and I will be more then happy to share our experience! Also, if you are planning a beach wedding, I would love to share our story for any nervous brides!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We Loved the Riu Palace Macao My wife and I just returned from a 7-day stay at the Riu Palace Macao (we stayed May 27 - June 3). We had stayed at the Riu Bambu last September and thought we would try the Palace this time around. In comparison with the Bambu, the Palace offered a much more relaxed atmosphere. The Bambu is more noisy and crowded whereas the Palace is much more calm and relaxed. The food was better, and the beach offered a beach bar where guests of the Palace could get drinks (at the Bambu, guests had to walk from the beach to a restaurant to get a drink). The Palace was beautiful, the staff was excellent, and the room was wonderful. When we first arrived at the resort, a manager assured us that they would do anything necessary to make our stay super or excellent - not just good, and they definitely did. The Palace is more formal than the Bambu; at the Palace, the men and women must wear something over their bathing suits, and the waiters get your sodas for you as opposed to the self-service at the Bambu, where bathing suits are permitted in the lunch restaurants. Also, the men must wear long pants to dinner at the buffet restaurant, which can be very hot. The buffet has a variety of foods, and our last night there, they offered lobster and filet mignon. We ate at the buffet restaurant every night, and you are assigned a seat and a time to eat; Angel was our server, and he did a fantastic job. By the third day, he knew exactly what we wanted to drink and brought it to us immediately. We never experienced any illness from the food - not this year at the Palace or last year at the Bambu. I sampled practically everything on the buffet, and never did get sick. Most of the guests are European, but the staff was able to communicate well with them and speak English with us. In fact, we were under the impression that the staff that spoke the best English had been assigned to the Palace as opposed to one of the other Riu resorts. The rooms were very nice and offered a mini-fridge that was stocked daily. There are hair dryers in the room, but my wife brought her own and asked for an adapter to plug it in. We had to pay a $5 deposit, which we got back when we checked out. The beach is absolutely phenomenal, and the water was very clean and clear. We got up early every morning and went to the beach. They had several canopies covering 2 chairs and a table, and we sat under one of these canopies every day. Most days, we fell asleep under the canopy with the breeze blowing and the sound of the waves rolling in. We also walked a couple of miles down the beach; it was beautiful and very safe. It was the most relaxing experience we have ever had. We experienced 7 days of total relaxation and had not a care in the world. We have stayed twice at the Moon Palace Resort in Mexico, twice at Iberostar in Mexico, and at Sandals in Negril, Jamaica, and we truly believe that this trip to the Palace surpassed those wonderful trips. We had such an amazing time, and we miss it already. We can't wait to go back!

<Content>lots of sun This was my fourth time staying at the Riu Palace and I have no complaints. I was here from 04/24 to 05/08 and it was extremely hot and no rain....bring lots of sunscreen. The food is enjoyable and the drinks plentiful. Thanks to the animation team (Johnny Bravo, Edward and Chocolate) for all the laughs. Take a scuba lesson with Enis who is here from Germany, very friendly girl. Robert the manager is very friendly and can be seen on the property at all times making sure you are enjoying your stay and that you are well taken care of.I think the tourists need to remember that the staff at these hotels work more than our ususal 8hr day and normally work 11-14 days straight, so if they seem a little tired, then they probably are. They deserve to be tipped especially if they are going out of their way to please you. If you want to shop ask someone about going to the Bavaro plaza as the Caribbean street is quite expensive, or take a walk along the beach to find many vendors. My only complaint is that this hotel is 80% German, and without trying to pass judgement, they seem to think that they are the only ones vacationing here and therefore tend to be pushy in the dining room and at the bar.

<Author>itsteve888
<Content>Riu Palace of Pleasure After reading many other reviews of the riu palace, i have to admit there was a bit of skepticism prior to departing, however, leave your fears at home. The palace is plush and exquisite. If your desire is to go to a ultra clean resort, with a very, very nice beach, a nice pool, great service staff, and enjoy yourself relaxing, this is the place to go. If you are going on an all inclusive trip to eat gourmet food, you may want to reconsider. The food is ok, not bad, just ok. I ate at the big dinner buffet once, and made reservations at the ala carte restaurants the remainder of the evenings. Myself, if i am paying premium prices to go to an all inclusive, i would prefer to be waited on by a server. Every meal i had at the ala cartes was very nice. You will need to make your dinner reservations every morning, for the same evening, those are the rules. A few other things to be aware of: if you can, close your eyes on the 30 minute drive from the aiport to the resort, it can be frightening. If you dont understand spanish, it can be a bit frustrating upon arrival, but dont let it intimidate you, within a day or 2, you will feel right at home. Approximately 50% of the guests are from germany, and i did not find them to be the freindliest of folks, maybe it is the 12 hour plane trip to punta cana that caused some irritation. There are 4 males that provide the daily and evening entertainment, and without any doubt, they are one of the reasons i would return, they are funny, friendly, and liven up the entire resort. The surrounding riu resorts are basically younger in age range and had more children than i would prefer, therefore, i spent most of my time in the palace. All in all, I would say that you would not be dissapointed if you want to go have a great time, at a very clean and friendly resort.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Totally Wonderful Place and Vacation at the Riu Palace Never have my husband and I received such excellent service as at the Riu Palace, altho' we take a vacation at least once and sometimes twice a year. The attention was incredible..felt like a royal family!! The place was so beautiful and immaculate and service people were cleaning up regularly. The food was very enjoyable, altho' the beef was a bit tough, but we ate kid (very tender), and at the carving station had a whole grouper (not that we ate the whole thing!), a pig roast one night (best I ever had, including locally done), loved loved loved the pork chops. Don't know what they season them with, but they were scrumptuous. Wouldn't mind having some of their recipes...!! We did eat at the International Buffet each evening as there was such a variety to choose from that we felt we would be cheated had we only one entree!! Our waiters were so attentive and after the second day, brought me my favorite, Cappucino, as we sat down, without me even asking. The bread was great and the desserts were wonderful. and this from a woman who is basically a light eater!! Salad selections were terrific, too. They also make great pasta dishes and pizza, of which I was surprised to find pasta there. There were at least 9 stations and on Mexican night, had addt'l stations. For lunch we ate at the Caribe Grill and/or the pizzeria. Both sit on the beach by the ocean and is wonderful to have lunch and sit and take in the gorgeous sights. Breakfast was in the International Buffet and choice of food was quite varied. The beach is incredible, too. soft powdery sand, no shells or rocks to contend with, did not blow on us even during one windy day,' walking into the ocean was like walking on velvet and, except for one day when there was a storm out at sea which produced some minor seaweed, was very clear and a beautiful turqoise in color. Had perfectly beautiful weather every day, but can't say that was the Riu's doing! HaHa. The service around the pool and beach is also exceptional. One day we were trying to move some chaises under the palm trees and one of the employees came up to us saying NoNoNo, and we thought, oops, we weren't supposed to move the chairs, but he meant, no, you don't do it, I do! He got us chairs and they also give you additional chaise pads to place on the chairs. We did also tip the housekeepers, waiters, and pool help as they do not make much money and truly deserved anything you give them. Each evening someone comes around to check the refrigerator which is stocked with beer, soda, water and the hard liquor bar, which had Beefeaters gin, rum, vodka and whiskey in. We are not drinkers, so to speak, but I like a drink before I retire to bed. The local people are very sweet and so happy, even tho' they have little compared to us and Europeans, Canadians, etc. We met some very nice people from France, Germany, Holland, Belgium, and altho' we always couldn't speak the same language, got our messages across. Due to some health problems my husband has, we only took one tour, altho' I wish I could have taken the Safari,. but one has to takewhat one gets! We also enjoyed the antics of the entertainment staff and the shows at night. We would definitely love to return to this wonderful island and hotel.

<Author>Kapfamily
<Content>An absolutely incredible vacation spot My husband and I, including our three young sons (8,7,3.5yrs) just returned from 8 days of paradise...Our stay was from March 18-25. We are very excited to report that the Palace is an absolutely clean, friendly, and high-end resort. The rooms, grounds and pool were spotless. The staff, incredibly friendly and would do anything to make your stay positively memorable. Things to remember: take plenty of your own analgesics,peptol bismal, suntan lotion etc, (not that you will necessarily use all, but better to have them with you, than to have to pay the high prices there); we did not see barely any mosquitos, but then again with young children we did not go out at night; bring lysol wipes, and in good practice, with any foreign place you are sleeping in, wipe down knobs, phones, tables etc; another good practice is to always carry with you a hand sanitizer; don't drink their water,not even to brush your teeth with.Get your Hep A shot; eat everything you want... expect as with any change of climate, different cultural foods etc, you may get gastric changes (in any part of the world). Sit back and enjyoy everything that this beautiful place has to offer, because the days will go by fast. Our children have visited the less primitive Island of the Bahamas, and to our delight enjoyed this visit more!(Were able to learn to scuba dive in the pool, banana boat rides, take pictures with parrots and monkeys). Again expect a high-end hotel, especially compared to the other hotels around you...don't get caught up on 5star etc, because the term 5 star cannot be used universally. Get there and ENJOY!!!

<Content>see you next year! We just returned from a one week stay at the Riu Palace and had a great time. The beach is beautiful and there is no problem getting a lounge chair. Lunch was downsized quite a bit because most people ate elsewhere. We found lunch at the restaurant next to the pool better than the Caribe Grill which is overlooking the beach. The wine is not very good if you are a wine lover but other positives more than make up for it.They offer outdoor massages but beware of the high pressure to buy a package. My husband bought a package of six and did not use two.Save your money and don't play the slots in the casino. Unlike Vegas where you know people actually win sometime these machines are very tight.Bring a lot of sunscreen, it is very expensive if you run out. Also don't forget imodium and pepto bismol. My husband felt sick a couple of days but was able to function because of the imodium. If you need to purchase any items you will save money buy walking three minutes to Carribean Street, items at the hotel shops are at least 20% more.Most of the guests at the resort are German, followed by other Europeans. We rarely heard anyone speak English. Most times language was not a barrier but it would help to learn some basic phrases in Spanish.Beware if you are going to go topless that my husband and I saw three different men secretly taking pictures of topless women, you may end up on the internet.The resort was constantly being cleaned inside and out. The staff was very friendly, this is a well managed resort.I'm writing this review sipping my Dominican coffee in my Dominican mug and wishing I was back at the Riu Palace. Overall we had wonderful experience and are definately going back.

The European cuisine was repetitive and uneventful. I'll take American food any day over that! We arrived on Saturday and by Monday many in our group of 160 were complaining about the food. We even went out on Monday and paid for dinner at a great restaurant on the beach that was referred to us by William at the hotel JELLYFISH. The food there was wonderful and Wanda  Gabriel treated us great. I highly recommend it to any who visit. I was very careful to drink only bottled water even for brushing teeth. On Thursday evening I had salad made with iceberg lettuce and tomato(the only thing my husband didn't eat that I did) and by the middle of the night I got violently ill with vomitting, diarrhea, headache and high fever. I was sick all the next day and could not even get out of bed until Sat morning. I was still feeling very poorly but had to vacate the room by 12:00 and wait for a 9:30 flight. Many peolple in our group got ill some mildly and some badly. Usa3000 was great, but the Apple Vacation planning was very poor. We were told by the Apple rep that the catamaran excursion was a 30 minute bus drive away. Two hours one way making for a 13 hour excursion. I have traveled many times and would not choose to go back to DR any time soon.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>No regrets Just returned Jan 22, 2005. The RIU Palace is five star in everything but the food and wine. The food is good but the menu in the ala carte restaurants is limited to only three choices. Since I like to be served rather then stand in buffet lines this was a little disappointing. The seasonings were outstanding but the meats were a little tough and fatty by USA standards. Most of the fish was great. I found it strange that most of the hors d'oeuvres were the same all week long. (shrimp, calamari, chicken legs, and fish.) Unfortunately we were advised not to eat raw vegatables as in salads due to the possibility they might have been washed in tap water. I do not know whether this is a fact since we didn't want to experiment but it would be nice if someone could verify this point since the salads looked great. The wine was not very good. There were only white and red and I have no idea what varieties they were. The room bar is nice and the local Presidente beer is a pretty good pilsner. Keep in mind that at this resort all alcoholic beverages are no extra charge including the room bar. Contrary to what I have read the bar and room ice is safe to put in drinks. You may want to take snacks since they are not readily available. The breakfast and lunch buffets were very good also.Service at the Palace is great and spreading $1.00 tips around is a good idea. As one person wrote on this site take a lot of small bills for tips. Special credit goes to the Hotel manager Roberto and the Headwaiter Salvador. They are amazingly friendly and helpful. Everyone at the property is wonderful.For a couple of days the credit card readers didn't work at some of the stores on the Carribean street. Some phone cards don't work. Verizon cell phones worked great with the CDMA network. Many other cell phones don't work. Check before going.The beach areas are some of the prettiest anywhere. The grounds are very well kept as you would expect. The whole place is constantly being cleaned. I don't know why but the jacuzzi and the pool are cooler than you would expect in that climate. The rooms are large and beautifully done. Our headboard was nearly 10 feet wide to accomodate two queens pushed together to make one of the largest beds I have ever seen. Most rooms have at least a partial ocean view off the large balcony. Room service breakfast on the balcony is wonderful. Due to the European design the bathrooms have a bidet but the tub/shower if a little small by USA standards. There is plenty of hot water pressure but remember not to drink it. Satelite TV is mostly Spanish but with enough US channels including Showtime. You probably won't need to watch much TV though.Apple Vacations did a good job coordinating everything. The USA3000 charter flight was a refreshing change from regular scheduled planes. They had real food and a movie. The service was good.Punta Cana airport is beautiful and modern. The only thing I didn't understand was the flight times. In my opinion they got us there too early for room availability and we left too late.Over all this is a great place to vacation if you like all- inclusive resorts. Be aware that the vacationers are mostly European and the beach has a fair share of topless sun worshipers. I hope this helps.

<Author>FilipBelgium
<Content>Stay from 1st --> 8 january I stayed in the hotel a couple of days ago. We had nice weather (a little rain from time to time) The hotel is rated 5* locally but I can confirm that it is more a good 4* compared to European and American standards. Overall the rooms are spotless but it is clear that they are used 'often'- they are cleaned once a day and towels are changed twice ! The pool is not big but very clean - the beach is superb (compared to the other resorts) - the spa is 'cold' but who cares, the ocean is warmer and it is more fun to swim in the nice blue water ! The restaurants serve very nice food. It is true that the food is 'European' style but I would think that this is a 'plus' since 'American' food in general (and I have been to your nice country / continent more than once so no hard feelings !) is not really the best is it? I havn't met any rude people (from wathever country) only some Germans tend to think that they 'own' the place, just ignore them. The staff is very friendly and will do everything that is in their power to make the stay as enjoyable as possible. Riu All-in means really all-in so no complaints ! I had a very pleasant stay, i didn't see rats or other 'cruel' animals not even a fly.... If you go to the Riu Resort the Palace is the Place to be; It is probably not such a good hotel when you are looking for a very active vacation or have younger kids, however if you want to relax and do 'nothing' but reading and sunbathing it's heaven on earth. I 'visited' the public parts (not the rooms or restaurants !) of the other Riu's in the resort (Taino, Bambu etc) and I have to be honest; I stayed in several Riu hotels all over the globe and only the Palace reaches the usal Riu 'standards'. The other hotels are clean but it is clear that their best time lies behind them. I hope this is usefull ! Enjoy your stay at the Macao Palace - Filip, Belgium

<Content>Relieved and Relaxed My wife and I just returned from the Palace and had a fabulous time. The Dominican is a very poor country and the staff at the Hotels put in long days and recieve minimal wages and have to deal with very difficult people. But despite these conditions the staff was warm attentive and helpful. If they could not help you they found someone who could. There were a few times I saw the staff deal with difficult guests with the utmost professionalism. If put in a similar situation I do not think I would have been as graceful. I am sorry to report that the difficult guests were Americans. The fact that Americans are the minority at the Palace was not a problem for me. This nonsense about rude Europeans I have read on this site is far from what I experienced. Again I am biased. I was stationed in Germany for 3 years in the Army and my wifes company is out of Switzleland where we have traveled a few times. I have found in my experiences that there are good and bad in most nationalities but what alot of Americans do not pick up on is that many Europeans (as well as Americans) find it kind of rude to carry on loud conversations in public areas i.e. pools, lobbies, buses, when there are others present. As far as the food you are not in Kansas anymore. The food was plentiful and varied. I especially enjoyed the theme nights. The Main dinning room was always clean and visually appeallingThe beach was beutiful blueand refreshing. The pool was always clean. There was always plenty of chairs umbrellas or palm trees to sit under. The only dilemma I had was whether to swim in the ocean or pool.The Palace was a great place for couples or families. There seemed to be a more younger crowd at the Bamboo or other Riu's, but I would take the Palace over them all. For the single folks there was plenty of action at the disco everynight. Other resorts had bigger clubs and if you wanted to really have some fun then you could try the local joints, just be prepared :)The only real problem I had was tobacco. My main complaint was I had to come home. <Author>name_screen
<Content>Riu Palace Macao great vacation We went to the Riu Palace Dec 8-15 with Apple Vacations out of Chicago O'Hare. We were quite anxious given reviews about illness, drinking the water, etc. We had a great time and completely recommend it, but we were very cautious with our health.Advice tips:1) Drink bottled water at all times. We used bottled water for brushing teeth and my boyfriend for shaving. 2) Bring anti-bacterial lotion and/or wipes. We brought both and used before eating and several times during the day. We also brought anti-bacterial body wash and sponges for the shower. Maybe we were overly cautious, but we didn't get sick.3) Riu Palace has the best food and drinks. We walked by the other Riu hotels, and although they looked nice, Riu Palace was better.4) Try to learn and use some Spanish. It was much appreciated by the staff, and even though we weren't always grammatically correct, we were able to communicate. 5) Bring lots of $1 bills for tips. We brought a stack of $100 singles and used them to tip the staff at the bar, restaurant, maids, etc. The staff was always helpful.6) Bring small bills ($5s and $10s) if you want to buy gifts, rum, coffee, etc.7) Bring an assortment of medications such as aspirin, imodium ad, pepto, bug spray, anti-itch, etc. I got a few bug bites and was grateful for the anti-bug stuff.8) Dress nicely for dinner. Most of the guests are Europeans and jeans  tee-shirts are not appropriate. Nice trousers and a sleeve-shirt for the gentlemen and nice pants and/or skirt for ladies with a top is fine. My boyfriend brought a suit too, but felt it wasn't necessary. I either wore black pants  tops or simple dresses.9) Food to eat: we ate only at the Riu Palace. We avoided any yogurt, mayo or otherwise creamy food. For lunch and dinner, we ate the cooked vegetables, fresh fruit, bread, cheese, rice, beans, chicken, beef and other meats without problems. We tried a few desserts, but honestly preferred the fresh fruit. For breakfast, we had eggs, potatoes, sausages and fresh fruit. Expect a European food spread. At the dinner buffet, it is self-service, but intended as a multi-course meal. Feel free to get your salad/appetizer, main course and follow it with dessert and/or cheese. We usually had a leisurely dinner (1-1.5 hrs) and we were frequently some of the last guests to leave.10) Outback Safari tour is fantastic. All day tour visiting rural Dominican Republic village, school, a home, a ranch for lunch, learn about coffee beans and cocoa, followed by boogie boarding on the beach. Highly recommended and well worth the money.11) Riu Bambu has the best evening entertainment. The Palace showroom was a bit musty with a quiet crowd. The Riu Bambu had a more casual, funny (albeit corny) and upbeat entertainment staff. The entertainment staff will make announcements in 4 languages (Spanish, English, German and French), but most of the entertainment shows were in English.12) Riu Palace was mostly German tourists, with a few other countries thrown in. It has a very European feel. It's a great hotel for couples; the Riu Bambu or Taino seemed better for kids.13) Be prepared to relax and have fun. We played beach volleyball, ping pong, swam in the pool, etc. We brought our own tennis rackets and played a few rounds. The ocean is somewhat choppy and not great for snorkeling, but it's certainly fun to float around.14) Lastly, bring lots of waterproof sunscreen It was sunny, hot and mid-80s every day. The prevailing wind off the ocean makes a nice breeze, but you'll burn if you don't take care of your skin.Relax, have a great time and you'll love it!

<Author>MariLand
<Content>A great 4 day trip -- a few advices. Just returned from our FIRST and very short (4 days/3 night) trip to DR. I cannot compare it to any other resorts in DR or anywhere else in the Caribean. I will try to give you some useful advice/information though.We went with Apple vacations. The service is great. The USA3000 flight from Baltimore is very good. It was about 3 hours. Apple reps are everywhere. They meet you at the airport and direct you to the transfer bus. Beware that the ride from the airport to the resort is VERY BUMPY, no matter how well and careful the drivers are. It's about 45 minutes long. The driver tries his best to make it smooth, but the road is not like your interstate at home.ADVICE #1: even though they feed you on the plane, take some food, snaks and water with you. You will need them!Riu Palace Macao is a very nice resort. If you usually travel in the USA, it reminds an average Mariott or Hilton (3 stars). All the rooms are in one building with a central lobby and several elevators. The rooms are big enough and very clean. We had a standard room on a second floor with a garden view (although you could see some ocean thru the palm trees on the side). It had two queen beds pushed together!!!. The room had a mini frige stocked with Pepsi line sodas (Pepsi, Diet Pepsi, 7 up, Tonic, Club Soda, and Presidente beer). In addition you have a liquor dispenser of 4 different kinds of alcohol (Rum, Vodka, Gin, and something else). We did not use it though. Also they provide a 1 galon jug of water.There are several resturants and bars on the property plus in the other RIU resorts -- all accessible by a short walk near the beach or thru the Caribean street.ADVICE #2: Take/buy some snacks if you'd like to eat something in you room. Or talk to the reception staff about the food once you arrive. There is NO food in the room, except for a dinne size plate of TROPICAL fruits. They are fresh and nicely arranged, but DO NOT substitue a meal for you especialy if you just had a long plane and bus ride. You CANNOT take any food out of the restaurant. (When we arrived it was 4pm. The lunch just ended and dinner did not start till 6:30 pm. The only food we had that day was a small breakfast on the plane -- and no snacks.) The same was with our departure: breakfast is till 12 and lunch starts at 1 pm. We had to leave at 12:15pm to catch our 3 pm flight.They serve you drinks everywhere: At the pool, at the bar, at the lobby, at the beach. But they serve food only in the restaurants. You have to get dressed to go into the restaurant to eat.ADVICE #3: Take some T-shirts and shorts or a beach/sundress for ladies to put over your swimsuit to go to the restaurant. You have to be dressed for breakfast and lunch -- no swimsuits or bare feet in the restaurants. (These clothes will also come handy if you need to go and use a restroom.)There are plenty of changind facilities and showers at the beach, but NO RESTROOM at the beach or the pool. There is one restroom at the Carribean gril that is at the beach. (We did not find any other ones.)The food at the buffett is good and plentiful. It is very international. We ate at both the buffett and the ala carte. Carribean gril is very nice and tasty. The stake house is good too (they serve only ribeye though). The taste of most of the food is similar to what we are used to in US, some is very tasty and some is bland. There are NO SAUCES except for the hot sauce and ketchup. NO STEAK SAUCE. The salad dressings are different in taste too. The choice of food at the buffett is pretty much the same every day, except for several items changing and also the theme nights. (We did not have a chance to participate in the theme nights though). The choice of food for lunch and breakfast is slightly different in each place, so try different restaurants if you get bored. We found that in the International restaurant by the pool, the selection was more close to home: they had pizza, hotdogs, french fries, chicken, fish, and pork and different kinds of salads, sides, and deserts.ADVICE #4: Try to keep the open mind regarding the food choice. There is plenty of food to choose from. But there are some items you will not find: No bagles and No cream cheese, No waflfes, No burgers, No fat-free milk, No packaged yougurt, No chocolate, No candy, No usual American snacks: like crackres, potato chips, etc.; No fruit other than tropical (they mostly had water melon, pineapple, bananas, melon, and some other tropical fruits), no apples, no pears, no berries, etc; Not many vegitables except for green tomatoes, cucumbers, carrots, cabbage and cooked broccoli.ADVICE #5: Palace surves everything in small cups. So if you'd like to have hot coffee/tea or a bottle of water with you all the time, here is an advice: take some insulated cups with you and pour coffee in them. The same for the water: take some water bottles with you and then refil them from the Galon that you will get in your room or at the bar.ADVICE #6. DO NOT DRINK or bursh your teeths with tap water. It is smelly and not filtered or purified.ADVICE #7: Take Immodium, Pepto Bismal, Tylenol, and other medication and sanitary products with you. They are available at the store, but very expensive. Since the climate and water is very different and there is a veriety of uncommon foods and there is plenty of alcohol and mixed drinks, you will most likely have some stomac adjustments.ADVICE #8: Do not be scared by bad reviews and by the malaria alert. Yes, everyone's view is different. Just be careful and use common sense. Eat and drink in moderation. We have not seen any mosquitoes at the resort. There were a few flies or bugs and lots of butterflies. The resorts are keeping everything clean 24x7 and treating the pool water and spraying for bugs.ADVICE #9: RIU Palace Macao seemed to be more couples oriented resort. They had a few kids there, but most of the facilities and activities including the KIDS CLUB are at the RIU Bambu. So, if you are going with the kids, go to BAMBU. We walked thru all of the RIU resorts there on the property and they all seem to be very nice.ADVICE #10: Keep an open mind and be patient with the language. There are lots of signs in English, Spanish, French and German. Most of the staff speaks or at least understands English. There are a lot of europeans at the resort and the staff tries to be helpful to everyone.ADVICE #11: The electricity is the same as in the USA. But you need an adaptor. You can rent one for a deposit at the reception desk. KEEP YOUR RECEIPTS for everything. To get your money back you will need to provide them with the receipt.ADVICE #12: There is plenty to do at the resort. The animation staff is very nice and frienly. If you'd like you can participate in all of the activities and use the water sports (I have heared that you need to reserve them 1 day in advance), or just relax and enjoy the beach and the pool. I do not know how it feels to be at the resort for 2 weeks, but 4 days is definitely a very short time!!!!ADVICE #13: Do bring lots of $1 bills. Although tips are included, it's a good idea to tip the staff at the resort: the waters, the bell boy, the animation folks. ADVICE #14: Do bring some small presents for staff. They like it and remember it too. We brought some items for the maid and left them for her every morning. We noticed that one time that we did not leave the little something in time (the service was done at the odd time), we did not get the same quality of service.ADVICE #15: Take a small bag or fannypack with you. You will get a room key, a safe key, and towel card. You will need to keep them with you at all times.Enjoy your vacation. Hope that this review helps a bit.

<Author>Complete_Travel
<Content>Good overall, but some negatives Stayed at the Riu Palace Oct. 27-31. Checked in at around 12:00 noon and they did have a room for us, although the air did not work, nor the phone. So we went back to the desk and were taken to another room, which overlooked a roof and was very noisy. So they asked if we could wait an hour and they would have a very nice room for us, which they did. Our room overlooked the pool and was very nice. We did have problems with the A/C, but found out that the maid kept leaving the balcony doors open which shuts the A/C off. The front desk staff was friendly and helpful. The resort itself is very nice, and it is nice to be able to visit the other Riu's to use the pool, restaurants, etc. The beach is good also. My husband and I really enjoyed the big waves (one day we spent 2 hours in the water). If you like calmer waters you have to head further south down the beach. The food was good, although the buffet did not change much from night to night. The Caribe Grill in the evening had a beautiful sea breeze flowing through and was a very nice atmosphere, the food was pretty good too. More variety on the buffets would have been nice. I was concerned about getting sick, but found that really there is no problem as long as you don't drink the tap water. They are very careful in the restaurants and bars and use only bottled water and ice made from bottled water. On the down side, we did not like the fact that you could not really comfortably leave the hotel complex. It was somewhat like Jamaica, in that it felt unsafe outside of the hotel complex. On certain days there was a lot of seaweed being churned up in the water. There were only about 20 percent American/Canadians. This meant that all of the shows, games, etc. were mostly in German and Spanish. Sometimes in French as well, but not too much in English. We sort of felt like outsiders. It is impressive though, that the hotel employees all speak German, French and English fluently! The casino is a big rip off! The slots do not pay out like they are supposed to. Even the dealers at the tables need to be watched. My husband thought he saw them deal from the bottom of the deck.

<Author>katendan
<Content>Great Vacation at the Riu Palace We have just returned from a wonderful week at the Riu Palace Macao (October 11 - October 18.) Hubby  I are in early 50's and this was our 4th trip to the DR. We have stayed previously at the Iberostar Punta Cana, the Iberostar Hacienda La Romana, and at the Fiesta/Palladium Punta Cana. We've also made a couple trips to the Riviera Maya area in Mexico. We had been booked at the Riu Taino, but for unknown reasons were upgraded to the Palace upon arrival. This was the best hotel we have stayed at in Punta Cana, and the service was outstanding.Our trip was booked through Apple Vacations, with a USA3000 flight out of Cincinnati. The flight was on-time and very pleasant, thanks to the friendly flight attendants who seemed determined to get us in a vacation mood. The food was above the usual airline fare, and included mimosas with the breakfast. Hotel check-in was easy  very quick. The room was absolutely spotless, lots of mahogany, with wing chairs and rugs beside the beds. Each room has a balcony with wooden rocking chairs, a table, and a rack for drying swimsuits. There is a mini-bar which is re-stocked with beer and soft drinks every day, plus a liquor dispenser with rum, tequila, vodka  gin (which we never tried.) We were amazed by the beautiful towel and flower arrangements we found in our room most days. Our maid was extremely friendly and always had a happy greeting for us. The evening turn-down service (and straightening of the bath) were a nice bonus. This is a beautiful place; the grounds, pool, and beach were just lovely. A few days there was quite a bit of seaweed washing up on the beach, other days there wasn't. We thought perhaps some of this might have been the aftermath of all the tropical storms this year. But the beaches are some of the nicest we have ever seen. We went parasailing, and found that you can bargain a bit as to the price. This was originally offered to us at $85 for 10 minutes, and we paid $70 for 12 minutes. Don't be afraid to haggle a bit. They also have windsurfing, catamarans, paddleboats, and snorkeling for free through the hotel. The water is warm and wonderful.We spent our mornings at the beach and afternoons at the pool and never had a problem finding a lounger where we wanted it. Eduardo at the beach bar was a very fun bartender; and Luis was very quick to fill drink orders at the pool. The people here work very hard, and we found them to be very eager to please, always friendly and smiling!There are five Riu hotels in the complex, and as a Palace guest you are free to eat and drink at any of them, except for dinner. We did go to all the properties for either drinks or meals, and found them to be very nice, although the buffet selections were definitely better, and more extensive, at the Palace. We had breakfast one morning at the Meleo and found the reataurant to be a little shabby. The Tainu and Bambu properties had very nice, active pool areas with pool bars that were very popular. We ate mostly at the main dining room in the evenings. We did try the steakhouse, which was OK, but the buffet had so many choices that we ended up there most of the time. There was a different theme each night, and always many beef, pork, lamb, chicken, seafood, and fish choices, even lobster one night. Do try to catch the Michael Jackson show one of the evenings that you are here (we saw it once at the Palace, once at the Bambu). VERY entertaining. We actually enjoyed the Bambu show more, as it is open-air (the LaBoheme Lounge at the Palace was pretty smoky). While we were at the Riu, it seemed that Americans were in the minority. We enjoyed visiting with our fellow travelers from Europe, and found the whole complex to be a great place for people-watching! There is a lot of topless sunbathing, especially at the beach. I came home with a determination to learn a bit more Spanish! However, we never had a problem making our desires known to the staff. Their English is certainly MUCH better than our Spanish. We did spend about $100USD in tips during the week that we were there. These people work very hard.We would definitely recommend this hotel to anyone considering a Punta Cana vacation. The staff here are the friendliest that we have met, and the most eager to please. Please feel free to email us at sniderd@wcoil.com with any questions you may have.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Travel Update I am a Travel Agt, recently returned from Punta Cana after experiencing Tropical Storm Jeanne (which became a Hurricane 1 Cat briefly, before downgrading to Tropical Storm). My husband  I arrived Sept 13 to beautiful weather and everything as expected at our hotel, Riu Palace. By Weds the storm had hit and lasted approx 5 hrs. We were perfectly safe as this is a solidly built traditional hotel. Debris, trees and other damage was obvious, but the hotel suffered no severe structural damage. We had power outages, no phones,no TV, and computer down time. The hotel had emergency generator so food, drinks, lights etc. were available fairly soon and the staff did all they could to help. Room service was curtailed (no maid service for 2 days). The most common concern for guests was lack of who is in charge?(hotel management here was somewhat remiss in keeping everyone informed),....and lack of Tour Operator presence. As An Agt I can probably explain that most Tour Ops on duty are local people and very likely could not get in, plus they have to visit and coordinate with several resorts. Also, the roads outside the resort were flooded so no cars or vehicles could arrive safely. However, I am aware this explanation doesn't always help when you don't know what's going on!After the worst of the storm passed (Thurs) we were able to walk the beach and checked out other properties beside the Riu properties - Iberostar Dominicana, Punta Cana and Iberostar Bavaro Suites. -- These properties suffered a lot of debris, broken trees etc and much flooding. Clean up was in progress, but of course it will take some time to get back to normal. The rain doesn't help! Overall comments at the resort were that the Staffs were doing all the could to help guests. But again, lack of Tour Op presence was a concern. Secrets Excellence resort suffered water damage and because of its location, guests were helicoptered out to the airport by Sat because of the flooded roads, for return to the USA. We had a Cleveland destination and were taken by tractor/trailer to the tour buses to dry land, and then bussed to the airport for flts out on Sat 18th Sept. As primitive as this sounds, I have to say that Staff/Tour Ops did what they could to make sure everyone was picked up safely and taken out. It is a point to remember that late Summer to end of November is Hurricane Season in the Caribbean and of course, risky for a vacation albeit a good price! We take our chances! I hope everyone involved this last week returned home safely and trust the situation is an experience learned. The Dom Republic does not have the infrastructure to cope with these situations as in the US. and I hope we give some consideration and appreciation to the people there who did all they could to help.

<Author>davector64
<Content>Water problem at first, but overall very nice Before committing to the Riu Palace in Punta Cana, I throughly read through as many Tripadvisor.com reviews on the Palace as I could. The reviews really helped me make a decision, as well as prepare me and make the trip that much more enjoyable. Everything from taking small US dollars, lots of singles for tipping, not expecting certain things we take for granted in the US and knowing how to handle certain situations.A little history to start; my wife and I are a pretty average couple, we're both 40 and have two young children (4  6) who did not go with us to Punta Cana. We don't travel extensively, but when we do we expect certain things based on how much we spend. This particular trip to the Riu Palace was booked through Prestige Travel in the Cincinnati Area for 4 nights with air and the price was well over $1000 (through the Vacation Express service). I booked the trip back in July and we were there Monday Sept 6th through Friday Sept 10th.Due to hurrican Frances the initial flight plan was re-routed through Atlanta but we arrived in Punta Cana only slightly off our scheduled arrival. The Pace airline service was excellent, there's no First Class on the jet, but the service and flight attendents remind me a lot of a Southwestern style airlines... not too frilly, just your basic charter flight with really friendly flight attendents. Once we arrived we immediately noticed the high humidity level, the tempatures for this time of year average in the high 80's. We left Cincinnati at 7:00am and arrived at the Riu Palace by 3:30pm -- Punta Cana is on Eastern time.Once to the Palace we immediately noticed the no windows, no A/C, all open and lots of vegitation all around the lobby and atrium terrace area. Ceiling fans are everywhere so the breeze off the Carribean is always apparent. Our room was very nice (on the top floor) with vaulted ceilings, tile floors and lots of dark wood everywhere. We immediately noticed the King bed was two full size beds pushed together and they were on wheels! This could make for an unusual situation, if you know what I mean! The resort is very clean, as mentioned in numerous other reviews, and the grounds are manicured daily. Even though it was hot and humid, it didn't appear to be an issue down near the beach or pool area. There were NOT a lot of bugs, typical to the Midwest States.We did have several problems with no water on the first day and no hot water the second day. A large portion of the water problem was due to the fact that we were on the top floor and the water pressure is very week up there... it even effects the efficiency of the toilet flushing everytime... yuck!! By the the end of the second day though, everything was good.As mentioned in other reviews, the food selection is very Meditereanian... which I thought was fine. I mean who wants to go to an International resort and have your standard US style food. I must say though, there's several dishes and desserts that don't have much flavor. One night we eat at the Caribe Restaurant out near the beach and it was simple magical... cool breeze blowing in off the Carribean and the service was excellent!The beach and pool areas are incrediable, tons of room and lounge chairs/recliners. It's funny, people would pull their recliners under palm trees or these really big bushes and fall a sleep for hours at a time... not sun, just shade! Unfortunately the beach bars are not so good, we had several drinks made from there and they were too strong or watered down. On their behalf I must say, they don't have a lot of resources to make good drinks in their little grass huts. The place to get really good drinks at the Palace is the Main Bar in the lobby area.... the Pina Coladas are excellent!If you're from the US, your only about 10% of the Riu Palace clientele, at least while we were down there. In the US schools had just started back up from the summer break and the vacation season pretty much had ended over Labor Day weekend, which is when we left.A WORD OF CAUTION, when out on a spending spree for souvenirs, keep an eye on the Peso to US dollar conversion (it's posted at the front desk). The water sport excursions and the shops on Carribean Street convert at different ratios, we weren't sure why this was the case... possible to cover a tax or a surcharge for using a credit card. I would recommend using US cash were possible. Avoid a credit card charge because they convert it to Peso's and you don't know what you really spent in US dollars until you get your card statement.... scary!To wrap up, I must say that we had a really good time! Heck, they even decorated our room on my wife's Birthday with balloons, flowers and even a bottle of champagne on ice!! Keep in mind, you are in another country and not everything runs like clock work (we take this for granted in the states) and just try to relax and not get too up-tight about the little things... ENJOY!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect Getaway My wife and I just returned from RIU Palace yesterday, and have to say that any negative reviews that we had read before the trip proved unfounded. The hotel was immaculate and the room we had was perfect. Upon arrival, I asked the desk clerk Raemundo, if we could upgrade from standard, and he placed us into a wonderful room overlooking the pool with a beach view. The veranda was great with the rocking chairs and the lounges, and the breeze was refreshing at night.The staff here is the most cordial we have encountered in quite some time, and we have traveled over the world for the last 20 years.The minibar was completely restocked promptly and the liquor dispensor was an added treat. The room was kept perfectly clean and extra towels was never a problem. Noise was non-existant.The main buffet was very nicely populated with any kind of food that you might desire. Breakfast would suit all tastes, and the dinner buffet was awsome.We lunched at the Caribe grill mostly, and the breeze coming off the ocean was a nice friend. The food there was the same each day, but the selections were varied enough to be fine. Lunch in the Mediterrean grill was equivalent, with the wonderful addition of pizza that was mouth pleasing.The Mediterrean grill ala-carte dinner was good(the lamb, in particular) but the humidity and the lack of breeze was a bit much. I suggest sticking to the Caribe, if you can get it, or the main buffet, for dinner.The drinks flowed freely, and never was there any extensive wait for service, we always got what we requested and usually 2 at a time.The casino is typical Caribbean, small and mostly slots. Keep your eyes on the card dealers, they sometimes get confused and in a hurry.The pool area was very nice and the water was a good temperature. Deck chairs seem to free up in the middle of the day when people either move to the beach or head for a snack. We did the beach in the mornings and the pool afternoons, and that worked fine.Caribbean Street is a nice touch, but we didn't spend much money there,,,we were here mainly to relax and just chill out.There is no pressure form the activities staff to do anything, and that is very nice.Now, for the best part! The beach is one of the nicest and best kept we have ever seen,,,,including Hawaii!The water was perfect and the lazy waves were great for floating on a blow-up raft. Lots of beach lounges, but you need to get there early to be assured of a spot under your favorite palm tree. Juan, at the beach bar, was friendly and would fix you up with anything he had at his disposal. We carried large drink thermos' and he would gladly fill them with ice and drink.The beach massage is something that I would heartily recommend, and it is really inexpensive.The single admonition is he same you will get from anyone,,,DO NOT DRINK FROM THE TAP!...we adhered to this policy and neither of us had any gastro problems.Besides, there is a gallon of fresh water in the minibar that is ice cold and refreshed upon request.We US folks were largely outnumbered, but that was fine, as we met a lot of interesting people from different parts: Spain, Portugal, Holland, England, Canada, France, Italy and Germany.Lastly, I DO tip,,,,and I freely do so for good service. you can tell when you hand a waiter a dollar or two that it is unexpected, but believe me, he(she) will watch for you and cater to your every need. Take lots of singles, they come in handy.We highly recommend the RUI Palace and it's sister resorts.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Riu Palace Macao tips for travelers We just got back from spending 7 days at the Riu Palace with my wife and two boys ages 15 and 17.This was a very enjoyable and relaxing vacation. I wish I had read some reviews before I went to get some inside info so that we could better enjoy our stay. My purpose in writing this is not to sensationalize or be critical, but to give some advice.First, carry small denomination currency for tipping. You don't need to tip a lot but I never had enough singles ($1) or fives($5). The front desk has an extremely difficult time making change, they just do not have american dollars and you and the staff don't want DR pesos. Secondly, bring your own reading material, magazines and books. The gift shop has German and Spanish magazines and papers but very limited English. If you like to bring coffee back to your room in the morning, bring your own coffee travel mug. It beats walking back up to your room with tea cups. We did the little speed boats with the snorkeling and it was great especially for my kids. Lastly, request a room facing the pool/ocean. We were in the back NW corner and heard garbage trucks every morning at 6:30am and again at 1:00am in the morning.

They were constantly cleaning the facilities and the beach to keep everything clean. They did have Internet facilities ($3 for every 20 minutes) if you want to stay in touch with people from home. We were on an Apple vacation and the apple reps were very friendly and helpful. A 5 or 6 day trip would have been perfect for this kind of trip and we would go back with no hesitation if we wanted this kind of relaxing vacation again some day. As for the drinks, you need to order a è„— frozenè„— pina colada, or daiquiri, or you just get the pre-made mix which isnè„— t so good. And ask for it with extra alcohol or it doesnè„— t taste like much. (We didnè„— t realize this until near the end) Only one beer to choose from, but this seems the norm at other resorts also. You need to order from the bars that have blenders versus the one near the beach which just had the pre-made drinks and beer available. Enjoy the beautiful beaches and palm trees! Hope these tips help you enjoy your vacation as much as we did ours!

<Author>WindsorSweetie
<Content>Great Resort, Great Time, Want to Go Back !! We spent our Honeymoon at the Riu Palace Macao in Punta Cana from February 10th - 24th, 2004. After reading some of the reviews before leaving, we were a little hesitant, but had already booked. From the minute we landed in Punta Cana we were treated like royalty. We were driving to the Palace in a luxury bus and greated by Victor Welcome Home as we entered the lobby. We were served a drink while we waited about 10 minutes for our room. Our room was spacious and well appointed and had every luxury we could ask for. It was clean and fresh. As we walked through the property, we were amazed at the cleanliness and friendliness of all staff. Our meals were more than wonderful, as there was every type of food you could imagine and then some. We had no problem with our lack of speaking Spanish and we tipped the maid a few dollars every day. They are most appreciative as they don't make very much money. We had the 8:30 p.m. sitting for dinner and got to know our waiter and tipped him the same every night. You would have thought he had won the lottery. Because staying at the Palace, you can visit all other Riu's near by, we checked them all out and ate lunch at a few, but never found the food to be the quality of the Palace. The other resorts were more geared to partying, so if you just want to veg out and relax (especially on a honeymoon), the Palace is the place. We did not have any problem with any gastrointestinal problems and they put fresh bottled water in our room on a daily basis. Nothing we ate or drank bothered us. Approximately a 15 minute walk in either direction from the Palace is a market place with items for sale. We found that we did quite well with bartering for the items that interested us. and found that the one to the left (if you face the water) was better organized and had more friendly owners. Claudia was our representative from Sunquest and she was amazing and helpful. We didn't do any side trips, but there was lots if you wanted. All in all it surpassed our wildest dreams and we would highly recommend it to anyone who wants a little luxury in your life. We want to go back as soon as possible, even wanted to stay on the plane and return the same day, but of course that wasn't possible (haha). Enjoy !!

<Content>Great place to relax We stayed at the RIU Palace Macao March 6-13 and had a very relaxing experience. The beach was very nice and the hotel staff was very friendly. In fact, most of the children we saw were staying at the neighboring RIU's. Also, we read a reveiw from someone who stayed here earlier in the year and commented on the drinking water and the possibilities of contracting intestinal problems--her solution was to take Grapefruit Seed Extract (GSA) as a prophylaxis. Half of us took GSA and the other half did not. Almost all of us had some intestinal discomfort/distress, not due to overindulgence, I might add. So be careful and take appropriate medications with you.In closing, just relax, leave your work and worries at home and you should have a good time.
