<Author>LadyDi95
<Content>Loved the Riu Palace Macao My husband and I just returned from our stay at the Riu (pronounced Ree-You) Palace Macao. Along with the other helpful tips posted here, just a few additional comments and helpful tips. The staff at the Riu was extremely friendly and eager to please. They are very, very hard working. We always saw employees scrubbing, painting or grooming the outside grounds. Each morning someone was scrubbing the outdoor tiles that ran through the open aired lobby as well as the outdoor tile walkway which ran across the back of the resort. The rooms are immaculate. Someone next to us at the pool also commented on the cleanliness, even indicating the maid cleaned under the bed each day and cleaned the patio door wall. I never checked under our bed but I took his word for it.When you get there, the meal thing might be a bit confusing, especially if you don't speak any Spanish. Just show up at either the 6:30 or 8:30 seating and let one of the waiters at the entrance to The Patio (indoor buffet restaurant across from the lobby bar) know that it's your first night there and he'll seat you at a numbered table. This will be your table for all dinners unless you make a reservation at one of the several outdoor restaurants on the property. If you want a reservation for dinner at one of the outdoor restaurants, you should let them know you won't be coming to the buffet that night. The time you choose for dinner will be your dinnertime all week. No reservations are necessary for breakfast, lunch or buffet dinner. No assigned seating in the buffet dining room for breakfast and lunch, only dinner. There is a no smoking section, so if you're a non-smoker and they seat you in areas with other smokers, just ask to be moved and they will easily accommodate your request. One other thing about the outdoor restaurants requiring a reservation, we were told if you do not show up within 15 minutes of your reservation, you could lose it. Buffet dinners, you can go anytime within the allotted dining hours. We ate at 8:30, and they were still serving an hour later. Definitely not as restrictive. Also, the food menu at the outdoor restaurants was the same each night, which some people commented on. We ate at the Steak House one night and found it to be ok.Food The food at the buffet has so much to offer that most everyone we talked to stuck to the buffet. You can't beat the selection. For all meals, you could choose from the following separate big buffets filled with: breads, fruits (melon, pineapple, mango, papaya, watermelon, etc), cheeses (6 or so selections), desserts, side salads warm potato dishes and veggies. For breakfast, add on the entire breakfast portfolio of offering; for lunch, add grilled, broiled or pan-fried beef, pork, chicken, fish, etc). For dinner, the same kinds of meat offering plus something special at the back buffet. One night it was roasted turkey being carved; another night it was roasted pork, another lamb. Well, I hope you get the idea. More than you could ever eat and always very tasty. One thing I will say about the meats, some nights, you might get something a bit overcooked. One night the beef might be a little dry, the next it was tender. One night it was the fish, the next it was moist. A bit inconsistent but overall, I just can't complain. Even the displays were absolutely wonderful. How they carve the different melons into animals and starfish is a real craft. I had to take pictures of the food displays.Dressing for meals Breakfast is pretty much shorts, lunch the same with a few people in bathing suits with a cover up over their suit. Dinner is supposed to be dressier, but I'll tell you, I saw some girls in hip hugger jeans that would put Britney Spears to shame. Guys have to wear pants but that's the only restriction. Women, just about anything goes and you'll see just about anything. Most are dressed appropriately, but some of the women's outfits I thought were not very appropriate. You have to remember all countries are visiting and some things may be more acceptable where they live. I think I saw one or two gentlemen in a sport coat and tie (that's it). Most of the time, it's business casual. For women too. Nice slacks and a top or a nice simple summer dress. That's what seemed to be the norm. One night I wore capri slacks with a nice top and I didn't feel out of place at all. One night I wore a skirt and dressy top and felt just as comfortable. I'd recommend no jeans at dinner. Leave them home, along with the Dale Earnhardt tee shirt. It just doesn't belong in a resort like this. Remember, you are representing your country when you go and it's bad enough Americans have a bad rap for being rude, overly critical and a bit on the heavy side.We read about a few tips that were very helpful. I'll repeat them here in case this is one of the few reviews you'll read.Tipping Bring a stack of one-dollar bills. We brought about 50 singles and used every one. Even though the Riu is all-inclusive, we still tipped our waiters and restaurant staff. I asked what they made there in wages, $95.00 a month. Some of the tour guides and outside help make 5 bucks a day. So if they are working hard for you, why not give them a few bucks? They never expect it, but are most appreciative when you tip. To us it's hardly anything, to them; it could be an extra day of wages.Bring a small pocket Spanish dictionary if you don't know the language. It helped us a lot, especially when asking for a toothpick :-)Pool and lounge chairs It took me a few days to figure out the game. I will save you some time. Get out to the pool at 7:00 am to reserve your chair(s). Yes, they say you shouldn't do it, but EVERYONE DOES!! The first day we got out there at 10:30 and guess what? No chairs were available. The next day I got out there at 8:30 and there were chairs, but no umbrellas. (Trust me, if you lay by the pool, you'll need an umbrella at some point during the day) So the third day I was out at 7 am and voila, my pick of chairs and an umbrella to boot. If the towels haven't arrived at 7 am, they'll be there within 15 minutes. Just put a magazine or book on your chairs until you get your towels. And hang something tied to your umbrella too. Don't forget to put something on your small table. I didn't mark my table on the second day and someone took it, even though' it was between two marked loungers. It seems so petty to have to do this but ..... and it's funny; everyone looks like little ants running to the pool between 7 and 7:30 trying to mark their chairs. Some marked chairs and didn't even show up until mid afternoon. Our week, the weather was so windy we could not be out on the beach because we would have been sandblasted. So the pool was where everyone hung out. Maybe if the beach had been less windy, the chair thing wouldn't have been as much of an issue because folks would have been on the beach chairs instead.Drinks Wine: 3 kinds, red, rose and white. Don't think you'll get a merlot or chardonnay or shiraz. It's red, pink or white. And it's not that great, not very full bodied. Reminded me of church wine. Wine selection, disappointingStrawberry daiquiri's, pina colada's, other tropical drinks: Disappointing. The daiquiri mix was bright pink (an early warning sign) and it didn't taste like a nice tropical daiquiri. No fresh berries either. I guess when I go to tropical places, I expect better tropical drinks than I can get at home. The pina colada's were not smooth frosties like we get in the States. And the bloody Mary mix was awful. The mixers here definitely need upgrading. Sorry.Side trip to Saona Island We took the trip to Saona Island, which was highly recommended by Funjet. It cost something like $78 U.S. dollars apiece. We left at 7:am and got back to the Riu at 7:30 pm. Way too long of a day. First you're bussed 1 1/2 hours to the place where you board the boats. It seemed like forever before we all took off from shore (yes, I'm another of those impatient Americans). Then 15 minutes later, we dropped anchor at a common snorkel spot. Whoever wanted to get out to snorkel was allowed. Time there, 30 minutes. They passed out snorkels and masks (which couldn't have been sanitized, pulled out of a plastic bag) to anyone who wanted to go. About 6 out of about 24 went in, including us. Then it was back in the boat and on to the next stop. Took another 1/2 hour to get going, pull up anchor and talk to someone driving the other boat tied up in the same snorkel spot. Next we stopped on a sand reef where we were allowed to get out and pick up starfish. I felt sorry for the same starfish being picked up over and over and over (every boat came to the same spot) but I picked them up too and took some pictures. Then we all loaded back in and finished the trip to Saona Isle. We stayed there for 2 hours. They had a nice lunch for us there as well. Bathrooms were available too. This island, which was touted as the most beautiful island was not even as nice as our beach at the Riu. Plus, they had the beach sectioned off for each tour boat that unloaded on the island. The lawn chairs were all on top of each other and the beach wasn't that great. After lunch, back in the motorboats which took us out to a catamaran waiting in the ocean. It was huge. About 50 of us loaded on and back we went. The trip back was exhilarating!! The water was so beautiful, shades of green, aqua and blue that I'd never seen before. The breeze in your hair, merengue music playing, it was wonderful. They brought out the rum bottle and Pepsi/sprite for anyone wanting some spirits. They also passed freshly cut fruit and a basket full of chips/munchies. The staff was very nice and some of them led folks into dancing. That's another thing about the Dominican people. They seem so happy and are always quick to break into dance. It was very contagious and they try hard to get you engaged to have some fun. The catamaran ride was worth the trip but next time we'd investigate renting a catamaran and just spend a few hours out on the ocean. Pick me up on my hotel beach to save me the 1 1/2 hour commute (each way). Get me back in a few hours and I'd be happy. I think they must want to give you your money's worth, hence the longgggg day. On the way home, we stopped at a store in Higuey where we could buy jewelry, cigars and other souvenirs. Much cheaper buying here than at any of the hotels.Check out/Return Our flight didn't leave until 11:25 pm and check out was at 12:00. They will keep your luggage for you and when you want to clean up to depart, they'll give you a key to a room that you're allowed to use for about a 1/2 hour. We took quick showers and changed. When we brought the key back to the desk, someone was already waiting for it.We got to the Punta Cana airport with a few hours to spare. We ended up taking off an hour early since the charters do such a good job of picking you up and getting you to the airport early. The arriving plane was early so we were able to board and take off without delay. Don't delay in getting to the airport when you're taking a charter. Also, they will go through all of your checked luggage by hand so don't use any chicken band ties (plastic, one-time use only) to secure your luggage before they have a chance to sift through your belongings. Instead, carry them in your pocket and attach them after they close up your bags.Last overall impression The Riu Palace is where you want to go when you want nothing more than to relax and chill out in a place that's well run, clean and a very eager-to-please staff. If you want disco's, poolside music and swim up bars, pick one of the Riu's next door. This place is quiet and relaxed, just what we were looking for. They will play poolside music, but only around 5'ish for an hour of poolside merengue (which they lead and teach). Quite a few participated too. They also offer a water aerobics class each day for around 30 minutes, archery and ping pong tournaments. The crowd is definitely on the older side. Average age is about 50-60. We met a lot of nice people but certainly not a rip-roaring party crowd. We are in our 30's/early 40's and were not disappointed because the crowd was older. One other thing to mention, we talked to a lot of people who stayed at other places along the beach. The one thing that folks liked most about the Riu Palace is that is was very compact. The restaurants/lobby/bar/pool are all within a few minutes walk. There are no great distances to cross to get somewhere. About the farthest you'll have to walk is down to the beach and that's only a few minutes as well. We liked the fact that everything was very close and easy to find. Even the connecting Riu's were a short distance away, though' we didn't venture over there but once or twice.I'd rate the Riu Palace Macao a B+/A-. If the drink mixers and wine were better and some of the meat less overcooked, I'd give it a strong A. A great place to stay and I would highly recommend it to anyone. When we come back to the Dominican Republic, we would definitely stay there again.

<Author>Perronss
<Content>Wonderful Just returned from RIU Palace Macao. There were 6 of us (3 couples) and we stayed 21-28 Feb.The place is fabulous but I will get to that later...I did a good deal of research on this site before I left, as you are probably doing now. In many other reviews of the RIU palace people mention getting bumped and overbooking. My group of 6 had no problems checking in and it may be because we asked our travel agent (Apple) to e-mail our desires ahead and we also e-mailed the hotel directly. We asked for 3 rooms together on the top floor and we got all that we asked for. However, we did meet a person who checked in the day before us that was bumped his first night but was comped for it.I have stayed at the Moon Palace in Cancun and thought it was the best ever. This place is many times better and much classier. Make no mistake that this is for the over 40 crowd who are vacationing without the kids for the first time (get the hint- leave kids at home with Grandma). There is not much for kids to do here and it is for RR, lying on the beach, drinking, eating, drinking, you get the picture.The food was absolutely first rate, all three meals. You can go ala carte to several places there. Mediterranean and steak house are good, Caribe not so great. The main Buffet is by far the best. None of us of got sick at all.This is the best beach I have ever seen for relaxing. Palm trees, beach bar, and perfect sand. The staff is attentive and will not allow you to lift a finger. They wait on you hand and foot and always have a cheery smile for you. The Dominican people are wonderful.Hotel is spotless, well kept and has a very classy feel to it. The staff is always working hard, cleaning, wiping, sweeping. You will see the same people for breakfast, noon, late at night and early the next day. TIP THEM. Usually $2 is plenty and it does make a difference in the service.Money--- Highly recommend you do NOT bring travelers checks. They are not widely accepted here and any change you get is in Dominican Pesos which are nearly impossible to change into dollars. Each of my group brought 100 one dollar bills for tipping and $200 in 5's, 10's and 20's. I met a fellow trying to change a $50 and had no luck. Bring small bills.Bring a travelers mug for drinks at the beach, the $5 one at Wal-Mart. Otherwise you will have to drink the 8oz plastic cups that get warm in a hurry. We took the Sanora Island Tour ($80 pp) and it was worth every penny.Overall I highly recommend this place. If you want wild times then look at RIU Bambu, next door. If you seek quietness with no kids and relaxation then this is the place for you.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>5 Days in Paradise We just returned yesterday from our stay at the Riu Palace Macao. It was absolutely breath-taking. The palm tree lined view of the ocean is one to be seen for yourself. We had a rocky start when we arrived, they did not have enough rooms. There were 208 of us that went together from one company through Funjet. We volunteered to share a suite with another couple which ended up being a beautiful one bedroom suite with a twin sized cot in the corner. After complaining on and off for several hours, we were offered a room next door at the Riu Bamboo, which ended up being lovely. We had our own room right on the ocean. The Bamboo is the hot spot, everyone from our group ended up partying at our hotel and pool anyway. The pool has a swim up bar and funny bartenders. Be careful of the dark rum, the pina coladas sneak up on you and make it hard to exit the pool! The food is excellent, we tried every restaurant at least once on all 5 properties and never had a bad meal. If you are not sure what's in the recipe, then simply ask and they will tell you. I read the previous reviews for months before we left and to be honest, I was worried about what we would encounter. Let me tell you, if you stay at this hotel or the Bamboo, you have nothing to fear! You will be treated like royalty. The grounds and rooms are immaculate. There are no bugs, we saw one wasp (in the flower beds) and a few moths. That's it, I never saw or got bitten by any mosquitos at this resort. We went on the Kontiki Clypso Snorkeling cruise. The best party ever! 5 hours of fun in the sun and the best snorkeling around. They pick you up and take you over to the Carribean Sea side of the Island. It cost us $50 US per person and was well worth it. They provide all of the gear which is well maintained and even have a resident photographer on staff to take your digital pictures in the water and out. We bought a digital photo albumn (100 pictures) 2 t-shirts and a hat for $37 US. Not bad at all. I would definately recommend this resort to anyone. You pay more to stay at the Palace and the only difference we saw between the Palace and the Bamboo was that if you book at the Palace, you get a wrist band that you have to wear the whole time and it gives you unlimited access to all 5 Riu resorts, which are all side by side down the beach. Speaking of the beach, on both sides of the resort there are street vendors where you can purchase souvenirs, paintings, cigars, etc. and since there are a lot of European visitors, they are all topless. If you do not want your children exposed to this, then leave them with the Animacion crew for the day. All shapes and sizes are mostly exposed on the beaches outside of the resort areas. Do not pack a lot of clothes, you won't wear them. The average temperature is 95 degrees during the day and 80's at night. The closer you are to the ocean the nicer the breeze. But that sun is very hot during the afternoon. You will live in your bathing suit and shorts or a cover up. Men must wear long pants at night for dinner, they can be jeans if you wish not to dress up. But you can always eat at any of the outdoor restaurants any time of the day in your bathing suit if you wanted to. A little Spanish goes a long way. They really appreciate that you try to speak their language. But you can get by on just knowing please and thank you. Do not drink the tap water! They will stock your refrigerator with gallons of water, use that for everything or you will be sorry the next day. Bring Immodium and some ant-acids and you will be fine other wise. I would have rated this resort a perfect 5 if they had not over booked our hotel. Relax, be patient and enjoy the views. Adios Amigos!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Think before you book....... My review of Punta Cana/Royal Palace Macao dated January 29, 2004If you are a seasoned traveler and have already booked your vacation, go and you will have a wonderful time. If you are looking into going my suggestion would be to wait for a few years before going. It is everything said in previous reviews both good and bad. It needs a few years under its belt to work out the kinks and develop further.I was a minority on 3 different levels. 1. I am a gay male. 2. I am an American. 3. I am single. Of those 3 possible obstacles I was surprised to find that being American put me most at a disadvantage. The majority of people there were Dutch and German. Americans are definitely NOT the center of attention there which although it was surprising I found it to be quite humbling. It was a nice reminder that the world does not revolve around the USA as we often delude ourselves into thinking.The drive from the airport was unspeakable. The level of poverty is astounding. There is definitely a slight language barrier. English is about the 4th language in priority there. I have a working knowledge of Spanish and even I found it to be challenging. My hotel, the RIU Palace Macao was beautiful. Pictures do not do it justice. It is immaculate, ornate, enormous and well organized. There are no ocean front rooms due to the situation of the hotel. The staff by and large are wonderful and incredibly hard working. I won t go into the conditions under which they work but will suffice to say that whatever MONEY you choose to leave them, anything, is richly deserved and vastly needed.The food is abundant but repetitive and flavorless. It almost seems that a special process was invented just to extract whatever possible flavor out of most things. During my 5 night stay I can say there was possibly 3 things I would consider good. Again, this is a result of the European influence. My friend and I do not drink so we cannot comment on the alcohol but there seemed to be plenty of it available including a cool wall bar in each room. The eating procedure, what, when, where and how took us 4 days to master. The maps and literature they give you at check in are all contradictory and inaccurate.Now onto the good news which vastly overshadows any and all small difficulties mentioned above .the BEACH, POOL AND SUN. These 3 things are outstanding!! If sun, beauty and isolation are your goals in a vacation, this is paradise. I spent every minute of daylight in the sun and water. I was so exhausted (in the good way) by the end of the day I was ready for bed at 9pm. It was utter heaven for a sun worshipper like myself. The beach is pristine, the water clean and gorgeous and the sun strong and searing, just like I enjoy it.I will write another review that will be more informative that will detail how to avoid some of the problems I encountered and advise on what you should bring, what you need to know to optimize your experience and any tips I have for future trips to Punta Cana. My criteria for a successful vacation is if I would chose to return. My 5 night stay at the Palace, all inclusive, including airfare from Philadelphia came to a total of $690.00 per person. I travel with my travel agent who obviously gets deals. For $700 I would definitely return to the Dominican Republic now that I know what to expect. I would not however return if a week cost me $1000 or more. There are too many developed and tourist ready islands that would provide more for my money.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>welcomed in the new year Our family of four spent New Years week at the Palace. We had two rooms....loved being on the first floor as we seemed to run back and forth to our rooms often. I appreciated the suggestion about the candles.....we burned candles on our balcony every evening. The balconies are wonderful....a great extension to a beautiful room. We took alot of $1 bills with us......they came in very handy when getting pool chairs in the morning. Every day I left our maid a dollar and a small bottle of lotion or candy. We had a few favorite waiters and we tipped them occationally during the week. The staff works so hard and they work very long hours. If you have a 110 v adaptor...take it along. Many of our US plugs do not fit into the DR outlets so you need an adaptor and during our week.....they were hard to come by. Take a travel clock along if you want to know what time it is in the middle of the night. The buffets worked out well for our family....young adult children who could always find something to eat and alot of it. Breakfast was actually our favorite.....loved the fresh fruit at every meal. We walked and walked and walked on the beach. It was very windy during our week so we were not able to use alot of the water toys because the red warning flag was out almost every day. Our kids took one excursion but we were very happy just hanging at the beach or the pool. There is a huge European influence.......we did not find many people speaking English during our week and that made it interesting. We enjoyed the casino a few nights. Our son enjoyed the ability to go in and out of the other RIU hotels and he met people from all over the world. We would be happy to re-visit the Palace.

<Content>2 weeks in the paradise My mate and I just got back from Punta Cana. We stayed at a gorgeous hotel, Riu Palace Macao. The service was good. <Author>Kinsa
<Content>The resort is great, but be careful if you book it yourself on the internet!! Overall, this resort is fantastic, really beautiful and the staff could not be more friendly. I got sick the second day (I don't drink alcohol so it wasn't that, and tried to avoid all meat for fear of getting sick, but still got sick anyway), and was sick for several days, spent 1 1/2 days confined to room. But, my hubby ate everything in site and did not get sick at all, so I really don't blame resort for my illness - just make sure to bring lots of immodium - you may need it!! The rooms are really great and first class all the way. The food was good for an all inclusive, but I have had better at an all inclusive resort in Mexico. Where this hotel really lacks is the specialty resturaunts, because the buffets get tiring after awhile.We had a fabulous time up until it was time to check out that we had any problem at all. This would only be a problem for people who book the hotel themselves throught the internet. Our reservation was for $180/night. We ended up paying what turned out to be about $210/night, because they calculate the peso rate equiavlent of $180 the day you check in, but don't actually charge you until you check out. From the time we arrived until the time we left, the peso devalued from 35 to 26 for 1 US. This means we lost out big time. I wouldn't have minded if this had been explained to us at the beginning, if we had been given the opportunity to pay upfront (we were not) or if we didn't have the reservation that clearly stated we were to pay $180 per night. After arguing several hours with the front desk people, who really were unhelpful, and quite frankly rude, we finally gave up a paid it (but we have disputed the excess amount with the credit card company, so we will see where that will get us - probably nowhere.) This really left a bad taste in our mouths for what had, up until this point, been a great vacation. I would recommend this hotel, only if you do not book it directly through the internet!!

<Content>Relaxing We are in our early sixties and we found it very relaxing. we were there 11 days which was great but the food did get a little repetitious. If you like mussels, shrimp and squid (we do), that is the place to be. there are a lot of other things on the buffet. We always ate lunch at the Caribe restaurant on the beach. We did have a hard time getting washcloths. You might want to take your own. My husband speaks some Spanish but we did a lot of talking with our hands. They really appreciate when the tourists at least attempt to say hello, good-bye, etc. They give you a sheet of Spanish sayings and it doesn't take a lot of effort to learn a few. We had a suite which was beautiful. We had requested an ocean view which is misleading because you can't see the ocean from any of the rooms because of the palm trees! The weather was great. The trip to Santa Domingo is not worth it - 4hrs. on a bus each way and we only saw 4 buildings and did a little shopping. It would be better to spend a layover there. Did go para-sailing which isn't nearly as scary as it looks. The Outback Safari is worth every penny and then some. At noon be sure to check what is going on on the walk from the hotel to the beach. They sometimes have special meals, band,etc. which was fun. They do like to have fun and are very friendly. We will return!
